Instead, we take ethics, ancient teachings, customs, feelings, and tastes and preferences as our base. On the surface some ancient teachings and family traditions appear to be the same as Christian teachings, but they are not Christ. We must turn away from all ancient teachings and family traditions. As saved ones, we have Christ as our life, so we must be rooted in Him in all things.

Enjoying Christ and
Growing with the Growth of God

Christ is our life. He is all-inclusive, He is the embodiment of God, and He is our God-allotted inheritance, so we should enjoy Him every day. Christ is in the Word, and He is the Spirit. The Spirit is the reality of the Word, and the Word conveys the Spirit. Daily we must read the Bible, which is the milk of the word. We must drink of the milk of the word daily to receive nourishment from the Bible (1 Pet. 2:2). However, we should not merely read the Bible; we must open our spirit to fellowship with the Lord. We must pray-read, and through our pray-reading we will receive the element of Christ. In this way the divine life within us will grow.

As a result, we will not change our behavior, nor will we rely on the cultivation of a preacher. Instead, God, who is within us, will give us more life. God Himself is life, and when the element of God increases within us, we grow in life (Col. 2:19). Due to our growth in life, we are brought into Christ in all things. This is what it means to grow up into the Head, Christ, in all things (Eph. 4:15). When everyone grows, the issue is the Body of Christ, which is Christ’s household and God’s temple, the church.

THE RESULT OF EXPERIENCING CHRIST

We must also preach the gospel to bring in new ones. Strictly speaking, it is a shame to bring only one person to the Lord in a year. It would be very strange if a peach tree produced only one peach in a year. In other words, a tree is usually laden with fruit. In the same way, we should bear abundant fruit. A sister once declared that she would bring eight to ten people to salvation in one year. As a result, in only six months she brought more than ten people to the Lord. In 1966 there were many junior high school and high school students, in their uniforms, in the audience of a large gospel meeting. It should be easy for teachers to bring others to the Lord. Those who teach in either junior high or high school have a good opportunity. The students they teach should be their “targets.” If a teacher has thirty students and is able to bring one-third of them to salvation every year, by the end of seven years many will be saved. This is a great undertaking. Every saint who is a teacher should not only learn how to educate his students; he should also learn how to gain them. Then his students will become his fruit hanging from him as a branch.

Leading people to salvation may be compared to a mother giving birth to a child. After giving birth, the mother still has to raise and educate the child. After we lead someone to salvation, we need to nourish him, and we also have to teach him. This is the way to have much fruit. If we are faithful to practice this, after seven to ten years, we will gain one million people in the Lord’s recovery. This is not a difficult undertaking.

However, we cannot merely produce numbers without the truth; otherwise, the new ones will be immature with no way to grow up, and the church life will suffer a great loss. Such a work would be of wood, grass, and stubble, and it would never be pleasing to God. For our work to spread, we must have the truth and life; we must also have the church as a support and as a home where the new ones can be brought. If we work in this way, there will be strong and living churches on the island of Taiwan that do not merely have large numbers but also have a proper testimony. There will be bright and shining lampstands. Moreover, the saints will be salt, and they will have a germ-killing function at every level of society. As a result, our country and society will be blessed. May the Lord have mercy on us so that we would be able to render our proper cooperation.

AN ADDITIONAL WORD

We need to have some fellowship concerning how to meet. When the time given for sharing in the meeting is too long, it is like giving people a large plate of dessert that is too sweet for them to eat. Hence, it is best to sing a hymn. We should sing with expression; we should not be too loud or too soft. Everyone must exercise to sing. Sometimes we can sing loudly, and at other times we can sing softly. However, we should not be habitual in our hymn singing. We must sing in order to bring out the flavor of the hymns. I hope that the brothers and sisters will know not only the Bible but will also know the hymns. Hymns are the crystallization of the truth. The young people in particular must learn how to sing the hymns. They should even memorize the hymns. Some of the hymns are on the central line of God’s economy. We must sing these ones more often, such as Hymns, #499: “Oh, what a life! Oh, what a peace!” There are eight whats in this hymn, and we should learn to sing them with expression. For example, the first two phrases of the first stanza can be sung in a strong way, and the third and fourth phrases can be sung softly. When we sing “Now it’s no longer I that live” the first time, we should sing it a little softer, and when we repeat it, we can sing it stronger. If we practice this, our hymn singing will be living, and the entire meeting will also be living.

CHAPTER ELEVEN

PREACHING THE GOSPEL
FROM HOUSE TO HOUSE

The Lord’s recovery is multifaceted, and it requires us to care for the truth, life, the church, and the gospel. In this message we will cover the gospel. Concerning the preaching of the gospel, there are three basic requirements: being beside ourselves, being thick-skinned, and opening our homes.

THE BASIC REQUIREMENTS
FOR PREACHING THE GOSPEL

The first basic requirement for gospel preaching is that we need to be beside ourselves. Prayer makes people beside themselves (2 Cor. 5:13). A person who has prayed thoroughly cannot help but be beside himself when he preaches the gospel. Even in other things, he will be beside himself, crazy, after he has prayed thoroughly. In addition to being crazy, we need to be thick-skinned.

The basic requirements for preaching the gospel can be summed up in two words: crazy and thick. We say this from our experience. If we are not crazy or if our skin is not thick, all our efforts will be in vain. We must learn to be crazy, and we must exercise to have a thick skin. We must also be practical and open our homes. The Holy Spirit was poured out upon all flesh long ago, but the shortage is that we are not crazy, our skin is not thick enough, and our homes are not open. We would like to fellowship concerning opening our homes. Even though opening our homes is not easy, it is the easiest thing we can do for the gospel. Furthermore, it is very effective. Opening our homes is very important.

Before we fellowship concerning opening our homes, we will study a few hymns.

NOT LIVING FOR JESUS
BUT LIVING BEING JESUS

The hymn “Living for Jesus” (Hymns, #456) was written by a famous American brother within the past fifty years. When the brothers in Shanghai translated this hymn in 1949 or 1950, the truth in the translated version was more advanced than the truth in the original. The first stanza of the original hymn says,

Living for Jesus a life that is true,
Striving to please Him in all that I do;
Yielding allegiance, glad-hearted and free,
This is the pathway of blessing for me.

O Jesus, Lord and Savior,
I give myself to Thee,
For Thou, in Thy atonement,
Didst give Thyself for me;
I own no other Master,
My heart shall be Thy throne,
My life I give, henceforth to live,
O Christ, for Thee alone.

In our translation we corrected all the inaccuracies concerning the truth that were in the original. But I would ask you, is this hymn really that good? This hymn is good, but it is not good enough, because Paul says, “To me, to live is Christ” (Phil. 1:21). In the Bible to live for Jesus is second best; to live is Christ is the best thing.

Regrettably, however, Christianity does not understand “to live is Jesus.” This is a point of debate between Christianity and us. Christianity is in the realm of for Jesus. Their realm is for Jesus, not is Jesus. I would ask which is higher, for Jesus or is Jesus? Which is easier, for Jesus or is Jesus? Those with experience can testify that for Jesus is very difficult, but is Jesus is much easier. This is because in “to live is Jesus,” everything is just Jesus. It is not I but He who does everything. It is He who makes the plans; it is not I who endeavors.

The greatest weakness of this hymn is that it is not written according to God’s central lane. Believers in Christianity are encouraged to give themselves to preach the gospel after every revival meeting. When I was young, we would sing “Must I Go, and Empty-handed” (Hymns, #930) at revival meetings because this hymn encourages people to give themselves to preach the gospel. However, this is for Jesus. It is not wrong to be for Jesus, but there is a shortcoming. We are not according to God’s central lane if we are only for Jesus. Being for Jesus causes people to veer off from God’s central lane.

God’s central lane is Christ as life, which is the Triune God dispensing Himself into us, His chosen people. Hymn #377 in the Chinese hymnal is on Christ as life. The first stanza reads, “Glory! Glory! Christ is life to me, / Glory! Glory! The Spirit leads me; / Weakness turns to power, / Darkness turns to light; / Glory! Glory! Christ is life to me.” This hymn is very simple, but it is on the central lane of God’s economy.

THE LORD DYING FOR ALL
AND THEREFORE ALL DYING

When we sing Hymns, #456, we will certainly set our will to live for the Lord. The second stanza says, “Such love constrains me to answer His call, / Follow His leading and give Him my all.” This speaks of a religious life in Christianity. Some people may say that 2 Corinthians 5:14 says, “The love of Christ constrains us.” This is true, but the entire verse says, “The love of Christ constrains us because we have judged this, that One died for all, therefore all died.” It does not say that One died for all; therefore, all were forgiven and redeemed. Rather, it says that all died. Christ died for us so that we would all die, not so that we would live for Him. Romans 6:5 says, “If we have grown together with Him in the likeness of His death, indeed we will also be in the likeness of His resurrection.”

CONSECRATING OURSELVES NOT AS A NATURAL MAN
BUT AS A NEW CREATION

There are some things that are right in traditional theology, but within those items there is always some hidden error, which is leaven. Let us take Hymns, #456 as an example. All the things spoken of in this hymn are proper, but there is also something hidden. If we sing this hymn repeatedly, everyone will set their will to “live for Christ” and “follow His leading and give Him my all.” Have we ever considered what our all is? According to Paul’s word in Philippians 3:8, our all is just refuse, and it is not at all precious.

The book of Leviticus, in the Old Testament, speaks of many matters concerning the offerings. None of the offerings recorded in Leviticus typify us. The sin offering typifies the Lord Jesus, the trespass offering typifies the Lord Jesus, the meal offering typifies the Lord Jesus, the peace offering typifies the Lord Jesus, and the burnt offering typifies the Lord Jesus (chs. 1—7). Where is the offering that typifies you and me? In the picture of the types, we do not offer ourselves; instead, we offer the Lord Jesus. When we feel that we are corrupted and sinful, we offer the Lord Jesus as our sin offering or as our trespass offering. We offer Him as food for God and for us as the meal offering. We also offer Him as the peace offering and the burnt offering. But when do we ever offer up ourselves?

Some people may say, “Romans 12:1 speaks of presenting our bodies as a living sacrifice.” However, we must understand the entire book of Romans in order to comprehend the words bodies and living sacrifice. Romans 1 speaks of man’s corruption, and chapter 5 speaks of the source of our corruption. Death and sin are our portion because we are in Adam. Chapter 6 then speaks of our death and resurrection with Christ—we are not the old “I” but the resurrected “I.” Chapter 8 says that the Holy Spirit is in us and that the work of the Holy Spirit is to sanctify, renew, and transform us. By this Spirit we need to put to death the practices of the body (v. 13). We do not put to death only the evil practices of the body; we need to put to death all the practices of the body. Only then does Romans speak of presenting our bodies in chapter 12. This word is not spoken in chapter 1. It is spoken only after we have become those who are renewed, transformed, and worked on by the Holy Spirit. The apostle did not exhort us to present our corrupted bodies. He exhorted us to present our bodies after they have been transformed and worked on by the Holy Spirit. The bodies that are presented have Christ and the Spirit within them.

Hymns, #456 gives us a natural understanding that we should live for Jesus, because stanza 2 says, “Living for Jesus, who died in my place, / Bearing on Calv’ry my sin and disgrace.” However, on the cross, the Lord Jesus did not only bear our sins and disgrace; even more, He terminated us. The apostle Paul’s word says, “The love of Christ constrains us because we have judged this, that One died for all, therefore all died” (2 Cor. 5:14). We have been terminated; now we are a new creation, and what we offer to Him is the new creation. But this hymn does not have this concept. It says only that the Lord Jesus died on the cross for us, bearing our sin and disgrace. This is entirely objective; it is not subjective. By the end of the hymn, what we offer up is altogether a natural man. Such a consecration is difficult to accomplish because it must be done with clenched teeth.

Paul says, “I am crucified with Christ; and it is no longer I who live, but it is Christ who lives in me” (Gal. 2:20). We must consecrate to the Lord the “I” who has Christ living within. A. B. Simpson wrote a hymn that says, “Oh! it is so sweet to die with Christ,... / Oh! it is so sweet to live with Christ” (Hymns, #482, chorus). “To live for Jesus” is an awful thing, and it is a suffering, but “to live is Jesus” is an enjoyment without suffering. “To live for Jesus” is altogether a suffering, whereas “to live is Jesus” is altogether an enjoyment. Living for Jesus gives people the wrong understanding and makes them think that they have to do something in themselves for the Lord. In reality, however, He does not want us to do so many things for Him; He wants us to simply let Him live out of us.

NOT GIVING OURSELVES TO THE LORD
BUT DENYING OURSELVES

The chorus of Hymns, #456 says, “O Jesus, Lord and Savior, / I give myself to Thee, / For Thou, in Thy atonement, / Didst give Thyself for me.” There is also a problem with the chorus. It is difficult to find a verse in the Bible that says the Lord wants us to give ourselves to Him. On the contrary, the Lord wants us to deny ourselves. Not only does the Lord not want our self; He even tells us that we should not want our self. Why would we give the Lord something that He does not want? Why would we give the Lord something He wants us to give up? Even though this hymn is very poetic, the truth contained in the poetry is not very high.

We should never think that discerning the truth is an easy matter. In Matthew 16:21 the Lord Jesus said that He must go to Jerusalem to be killed and on the third day be raised. When Peter heard this, he took the Lord aside and began to rebuke Him, saying, “God be merciful to You, Lord! This shall by no means happen to You!” (v. 22). If we had been there, we would have shouted Amen and thought that Peter was right. But the Lord answered, “Get behind Me, Satan!” (v. 23). Then He continued, “If anyone wants to come after Me, let him deny himself” (v. 24). Hence, the Bible clearly tells us to deny ourselves; it does not want us to give ourselves to the Lord.

Perhaps some would say that Romans 6:13 says, “Neither present your members as weapons of unrighteousness to sin, but present yourselves to God as alive from the dead, and your members as weapons of righteousness to God.” They think that this verse speaks of presenting ourselves to God, but if we consider the context of this verse, we will see that yourselves does not refer merely to us as those who have been raised from the dead; it refers also to our members. Our members are part of our body. Romans 6 deals with the problem of sins. Sinning is mainly a matter of the body. Verse 6 says, “Knowing this, that our old man has been crucified with Him in order that the body of sin might be annulled, that we should no longer serve sin as slaves.” This chapter refers to our bodies being put to death by the cross. Hence, yourselves in Romans 6 refers to our bodies. The Scripture is clear about this to the extent that it mentions not only “body” but also “members.” This means that yourselves in this chapter does not refer to the soul, the self.

Myself in the chorus of Hymns, #456 refers mainly to the person in our soul, not to our body. Strictly speaking, we cannot give ourselves to the Lord; we must instead put ourselves aside. This is what Paul says in Galatians 2:20: “I am crucified with Christ; and it is no longer I who live, but it is Christ who lives in me.” The I, the self, in this hymn does not refer to the body but to the person, which is our natural I, the soul-life.

LETTING CHRIST LIVE IN US

If we do not have a basic knowledge of the truth when we read this hymn, we will gain a wrong understanding. The hymn says that we must give ourselves to live for Christ. To live for Christ is an erroneous concept. It is not that we live for Christ; it is that we let Christ live in us. Then, in our bodies we need to cooperate with the Lord and allow Him to direct us. According to what is written in Romans 6, when we present our bodies to be under His direction, we are offering our members to God (v. 13).

If we do not have the light of the truth when we sing this hymn, we will offer ourselves to God and think that we can do something great for Him. One of the problems in Christianity is that before believers give themselves to God, they do not have many difficulties. But as soon as they consecrate themselves to God, they have problems that result in divisions and produce many sects. Therefore, we must remember that we must not bring our “self” with us when we love the Lord. We should never think that after we have consecrated ourselves, we must live for Jesus from then on, nor should we want to accomplish something for Him. If we do this, we will fall into trouble, and after ten years the full-time serving ones would be divided into five or six different groups.

We should not consider living for Christ; instead, we must realize that we have already been crucified with Christ, that we have died, and that it is Christ who lives in us. We should not be persons who live for Christ; rather, we should be persons to whom to live is Christ. “Because we have judged this, that One died for all, therefore all died” (2 Cor. 5:14). If we have died, how can we still live? We must remember that we have all died. However, every way that we take in resurrection is a living way with a tremendous future because Christ is living in us. In ourselves, we are at a dead end. However, because Christ is living in us, we are full of hope and have a bright future.

If the young people have the slightest misconception concerning Hymns, #456, they will get into trouble. Anyone who is sixty-five years and over, however, will have a heart filled with so much gratitude that they will think it is sufficient just to have the opportunity to love the Lord, and they will be satisfied simply to serve Him in the church. The older ones do not really want to go out and do something great. Those who have been called by the Lord to serve Him full time for their entire lives have a wonderful testimony. Just as Judges 5:15 and 16 say, they have great resolutions in heart and great searchings of heart. But when we see some with such a lofty desire, there is also some concern because we fear that as “wild oxen” and “wild asses” they will desire to live for Jesus and want to accomplish something great. We fear that they will destroy the church. I say this because of lessons we have learned in the past.

TAKING WARNINGS FROM OUR HISTORY

In 1949 we came to Taiwan to start the work. Before then I was in Shanghai, where we had gained a group of young people, most of whom were students, and some had been saved through my preaching of the gospel. Later, when the political situation in the country changed, I was sent to Taiwan according to the arrangement in the work. At that time, Brother Nee fellowshipped with me that if at all possible, he wanted the group of young people who were under my leading in Shanghai to go to Taiwan. As transportation became available, more than ten of those young people came to Taiwan to receive my leading.

Around 1958 these saints felt that their wings had grown and that they could fly, so they told people, “Brother Lee is finished, and the brothers who serve with him are ready to be put into coffins.” When I later returned to Taiwan after visiting England and Denmark, these saints were busy meeting in secret, but on the surface they pretended to be under my leading. Many saints were not clear about what they were doing, and even I was not clear.

One of the brothers who served with me in Taipei went to visit the church in Chiayi, and while he was there, this group seized the opportunity to meet with him and tried to persuade him to stand with them. When he returned to Taipei, he fellowshipped with a second brother, and the two decided to invite the young brothers to Taipei. When the young brothers were in Taipei, they were even more open and bold in their attempt to persuade the two brothers to join them in their rebellion. During this time Sister Lee was critically ill, so the two brothers did not tell me anything. In April 1959, after Sister Lee had passed away, as I was preparing to visit the Philippines, the two brothers from Taipei came to see me. They did not feel that it was right for me to leave for the Philippines without knowing the situation with those young brothers. After listening to their fellowship, I told them that according to the principle of the work, those brothers should be stopped from participating in the work. This did not mean that they would be excommunicated from the church; they would still be brothers in the church. However, since they were under my leadership in the work, I had the position and responsibility to stop them from continuing in the work.

I immediately called a meeting in May 1959 of all the co-workers in Taiwan and fellowshipped with them concerning my fellowship with the two brothers from Taipei. I said, “Among us one hundred co-workers, there are some who strongly disagree with the work and want to take another way. I would like to tell you that the way I am taking and the work under my leadership will continue; I will absolutely not make any change. If you feel that you have seen something, and if you feel that your way is superior, I hope that you will take your way and not stay here waiting for me to change. I cannot and will not change. I hope you are all clear that we are all brothers in the Lord, and even though I was the one who led you in the beginning, we are still all brothers. But I ask you not to remain here pretending that you are one with me. My position and my resolve are that I will not change. I will continue taking this way. This is the way that Brother Nee helped me to walk, and I will continue to take this way. This is my position.”

During the meeting the two brothers who had fellowshipped with me asked me to be merciful toward the young brothers, saying that because they were still young, they should be given another chance. Some of the older brothers also felt that I should be broad toward the young brothers and give them some time. Hence, I left for the Philippines without any further dealing related to this matter.

At the end of 1959, I held a training in Taipei on the Life-study of the Gospel of John. We had one or two conference meetings a week. During this training I spoke only concerning the first two chapters of John, after which I felt that I should not speak further. As a conclusion I said, “In John 2:19 the Lord said, ‘Destroy this temple, and in three days I will raise it up.’ I know for sure that there are several co-workers here who are doing a destroying work. I would like to tell you that if the work in Taiwan is the Lord’s, He will rebuild this work in resurrection, regardless of how much you destroy it.” From that day on, I did nothing more—I tolerated them.

In 1960 I went to America, and I visited several places the following year. I stayed in America for quite some time. After a great deal of consideration, I realized that the Lord had given me a burden, and that He wanted me to stay in America to begin the work of the Lord’s recovery there. I stayed in America from 1961 through 1965; that was a period of about four years. During those four years, the two brothers from Taipei wrote me every one or two weeks concerning the dissenting brothers. In response I always told the brothers to be at peace and to allow the dissenting brothers to do what they could to tear down the work.

In April 1965 the letter I received from the two brothers in Taipei was different from their previous letters. They said that I was the only one with the standing to say anything, and that all the co-workers felt that there was no way for them to continue in the work. I immediately wrote them saying that I would return to Taiwan in September to deal with the matter. In my letter I asked the brothers to make arrangements for me to hold a co-workers’ meeting the day after I arrived. The first item on the agenda for that meeting was to deal with the problem.

I returned to Taiwan in September, and on the following morning there was a meeting of all the co-workers in Taiwan. At the beginning of the meeting I said, “Four of you sitting here have been doing a subversive work ever since I left Taiwan. Hence, I am asking you four to withdraw from the work as of today.”

At noon the following day, two of the four came to speak with me at the workers’ home. I said to them, “Brothers, what is there to speak about?” They insisted on speaking with me, so the three of us sat down and talked in a small sitting room. One of them said that they did not have any problems with the work, nor with the way of the church, nor with my leadership, nor my authority in the Lord’s work. I responded, “Brother, is this really true?” He said, “We have no problems.” I said, “This is hard to accept because more than eighty co-workers say that you have a problem.” He responded, “The two brothers from Taipei made up all the stories about us, and they asked you to come back so that you would be forced to do this to us.” This troubled me. They had been undermining the work for many years, and now they were trying to blame others. I asked myself how the church could accept this. Their words confirmed my initial feeling to stop them from participating in the work.

Since the two dissenting brothers insisted that they had no problems with anything in the churches, I asked them how they could explain that the four localities in which they served—Taipei, Chiayi, Tainan, and Kaohsiung—had not sung any of the eighty-five new hymns for the past four years, even though all the other localities enjoyed these hymns. This question muzzled their mouths. They were also unable to answer other questions. Hence, I said, “Brothers, this situation is a fact. I ask you brothers to withdraw from the work from now on, but you may still attend the church meetings and function as brothers.” They brought up the matter of the eldership, and I told them that they also had to withdraw from the eldership; otherwise, the problems would not have a clear resolution. They could stand in the position of brothers and do their best to be good brothers. If they would give the Lord some time, He would vindicate them.

BUILDING UP THE BODY OF CHRIST

It is precious to consecrate ourselves to serve full time, but we must not bring in our natural life. There used to be many co-workers. After we were raised up by the Lord, none of us had any desire to do anything for ourselves. We all had only one goal—the Lord’s recovery. Therefore, we did not have any problems, and no one played tricks in the Lord’s recovery. I led the church in a certain locality, building up the church there, but I never felt that the church was built up by me, or that it was in my pocket. I did not have such a feeling. We all had such a spirit, following the footsteps of Brother Nee’s leadership.

However, with time there were some who had difficulties. Some saints came into the Lord’s recovery, expecting to find an opportunity to promote themselves. When they were unable to promote themselves, they left us and became preachers in Christianity. Several of the famous Chinese preachers were with us for a time and then turned away to establish their own work. I believe they know that the way they are taking is not right. They know that there is only one church. But they were forced to begin another work because they wanted to do something for themselves.

In 1965 I spoke a word of warning to a few brothers who wanted to leave the Lord’s recovery. I told them that not long after they leave they would divide again and again, because they rejected the ground of the church. My warning to those brothers has been fulfilled. They did not just separate themselves from others, they also divided among themselves again and again. All of you who serve full time must know that your serving is truly of the Lord, and it is precious that you have received grace and are willing to serve full time. However, you must take this warning and be inoculated. You should not think that you can consecrate yourselves to live for the Lord; you should not have great resolutions or great searchings in yourselves. On the contrary, you must always remember that the Lord has only one work on this earth, and that work is to build up His Body. There is only one church in the universe, and there is only one expression of that church in a locality.

You can do your best to develop the gifts that you have received from the Lord, and there is absolutely no restriction in the Lord’s recovery concerning this matter. However, you must adhere to the one principle of not doing any other work and not using gimmicks in the Lord’s recovery. You should only carry out your function. Do not say that you have built up a church, and do not consider any church as your church. Every church is the Lord’s.

By the Lord’s mercy the church in Chefoo was built up mainly through my ministry; however, I never considered the church in Chefoo to be my personal church. At a certain point in time, the Lord raised up an environment that forced me to leave Chefoo. When I left, I did not give anyone instructions concerning the church and the work. I simply told the responsible brothers that I had to leave, and I left. After China won the Sino-Japanese War, the Lord led me to Shanghai, and I ministered there for two and a half years. This brought in a revival to the church. Even though I was taking the lead, none of the church affairs were in my hand. Hence, when the time came for me to leave, I got on a plane and left. That was also the situation when I left Taiwan to go to America. No matter where I am, I always serve in coordination with the local brothers.

We must always remember this principle: we are here only to labor and to expend our energy in the Lord’s recovery to build up His Body. We want to explain this matter clearly to the young people because we hope that you will not have ambitions or great aims. We hope that you would simply be faithful and live Christ in every circumstance. You must gain people for the Lord, build them up, and perfect them. Everything you do must be for the church in your locality. No local church belongs to you or to me. Every local church belongs to Christ, to God, and to the saints. In the New Testament there are three designations for the church: the church of God (1 Cor. 1:2; 10:32), the church of Christ (Rom. 16:16), and the church of the saints (1 Cor. 14:33). No church belongs to an apostle, no church belongs to an elder, and no church belongs to a co-worker. The church belongs to the saints, and we should only take the position of being one of the many saints enjoying the church. Perhaps some churches were raised up through our work, or some saints were saved through our work, but those churches are still the churches of the saints.

PROMOTING THE GOSPEL IN THE HOMES
BY PREACHING FROM HOUSE TO HOUSE

Acts 5:42 says, “Every day, in the temple and from house to house, they did not cease teaching and announcing the gospel of Jesus as the Christ.” Recently, a Roman Catholic organization put out a publication that praised us, because we practiced serving in homes and in small groups before 1958. The author felt that such a practice is very effective.

Before 1958 every move we took in leading the church was according to the Bible. We had home meetings based on the expression from house to house in Acts 5:42 and 2:46. In Shanghai and in Chefoo we met in the homes, but we did not meet in groups. Later, when we came to Taiwan, the number of saints increased rapidly, and it was not enough to divide into homes; we also had to have groups. The practice of meeting in groups is based on the record in Luke 9 where the Lord fed five thousand people with five loaves and two fish. In that chapter the Lord said, “Make them recline in groups of about fifty each” (v. 14). The Greek word for group refers to a small unit or company.

When the church in Taipei first began to practice meeting in groups, there were not many saints in each group; there were only about twenty. Then later, the numbers gradually increased until a group had as many as one hundred saints. After much practice and observation, we needed to reduce the numbers in our groups. According to the Bible, twelve people can be considered a group, because the first group of early disciples was the twelve apostles. There are about fifteen thousand saints in the church in Taipei, and about five thousand of these meet regularly. There are usually three or four thousand saints meeting every Lord’s Day. If we were to form groups of twelve, the entire church in Taipei could meet in three to four hundred groups. The groups should not be formed according to the spiritual level of the saints but according to their residential location. The principle of meeting from house to house is to split up into groups. As soon as we are in groups, it is easy to shepherd, teach, and care for others in a detailed way. This is the basic unit for our future development.

Acts speaks of preaching the gospel from house to house. When the early disciples preached the gospel, they did not preach only in the temple but also in the homes. Every brother and sister opened his or her home for the preaching of the gospel, and they invited their relatives, friends, and neighbors. Every household preached the gospel. If we cannot preach the gospel every week, we should do it at least every other week or once a month.

At this point we must commend the sisters, because the gospel in the homes is built on the sisters for the following reasons. The brothers are busier during the day because they go out to work; their hearts are not necessarily concerned with the homes. The sisters are the stronger ones in the church in the matter of loving the Lord. The Bible records two instances of sisters anointing the Lord with fragrant ointment; one is in Luke 7:36-39, and the other is in Matthew 26:6-13. The brothers were rational, cold, and calculating, so they thought that the fragrant ointment could be sold for much money, which could be given to the poor. Hence, the gospel in the homes should not be committed to the brothers. We must let the sisters take care of it. We must motivate the sisters. Furthermore, people are more likely to refuse an invitation from the brothers, but they will feel somewhat embarrassed to refuse an invitation from the sisters. Hence, we must emphasize the function of the sisters in promoting the preaching of the gospel in the homes until every home is open for the gospel.

The brothers who serve with the name lists of those in the church should tell us how many household units there are. If the church in Taipei has twelve hundred households, it means that there are twelve hundred gospel stations in the church. If every one of these twelve hundred homes can gain an average of three people per year, then the entire church can save thirty-six hundred people in a year. I have the assurance that if all the saints faithfully receive this commission, the church in Taipei will be able to double its number in the near future.

THE GOSPEL WORK IN THE SCHOOLS

We also need to take care of the work in the schools. The city of Taipei has about one hundred twenty thousand university students, eighty thousand technical college students, fifty thousand high school students, and one hundred forty thousand junior high school students. This adds up to a total of almost four hundred thousand students. The young brothers and sisters who serve full time should be assigned to preach the gospel in the schools. They do not need to do anything else. They need to do only this one thing: preach the gospel from morning to night on the campuses. It is easy for one household to save three people in a year. But how many people can a full-timer serving on the campus save? If every full-timer saves an average of ten people in a year, four hundred full-time brothers and sisters will be able to save four thousand people in one year. By doing only the campus work, we should be able to gain four thousand new believers.

THE CHILDREN’S GOSPEL WORK

Another item is the children’s gospel work. We should assign at least ten full-time serving ones to concentrate on the children. It would be best for most of them to be sisters. At present, no more than five hundred children come to the meetings. We hope that we can increase this number to one thousand. The children’s meetings should be carried out in the homes. There should not be more than twelve children in a class, and they can have three high school sisters or brothers as their teachers. The full-time co-workers should promote this work, prepare the teaching materials, and take care of all the other matters.

Every children’s home meeting should frequently preach the gospel and invite their relatives and the children of their neighbors. Even though some parents will not come, they will allow their children to come. We believe that many people will be brought in through the children’s gospel work. I hope that we will have two thousand children by next spring, three thousand by the summer, and four thousand by next fall. There is a great future in this work. If we take this way, there will be ten thousand children in the church in Taipei within two to three years. At least two to three thousand children out of the ten thousand will not be the children of the saints. The children’s meetings will open up a way to gain people, especially the parents of the other children.

THE GOSPEL WORK AT ALL LEVELS OF SOCIETY

In addition, we can gain people from different professions in society, such as those who work in hospitals, government offices, factories, and businesses. It is very probable that we can add five to ten thousand people every year. This requires us to maintain the two great pillars of preaching the gospel from house to house and preaching the gospel in the schools.

Apart from these ways to preach the gospel, we must use the small groups to recover the dormant brothers and sisters. There are approximately ten thousand dormant saints. If we are faithful, within six months we will recover one-third of them. This can bring in another three thousand people.

OPENING EVERY HOME FOR THE UNIVERSAL
SPREADING OF THE GOSPEL

We must pay particular attention to opening the homes for the gospel. Opening one’s home to preach the gospel must become a universal practice. Every saint’s home must be open for the gospel. Even a newly baptized saint can open his home for the gospel. The saints who have recently been baptized are fresh, and they have many friends and relatives. If they invite their friends and relatives to their homes, it will be easy to gain them.

We must change our concepts and not think that a “spiritual” household will be more effective in preaching the gospel. This is not necessarily true. On the contrary, sometimes a household that is too spiritual does not bear fruit. In general, people have children when they are young and strong. Hence, our view must change. We must see that even newly saved ones can preach the gospel to gain others. Of course, we are not saying that the saints should not be spiritual, nor are we encouraging the saints to love the world. We are saying that there is no need to be tied down by conventions. We should not be influenced by different situations; rather, we should just do our best to preach the gospel.

We must come to the Bible to see how the Lord Jesus preached the gospel. The Lord Jesus went to the homes of tax collectors and sinners. He did not go merely to preach the gospel; He also sat down to eat with the tax collectors and sinners. He said, “Those who are strong have no need of a physician, but those who are ill” (Matt. 9:12). The Lord was saying, “Pharisees, if you think that you are not ill, I can have nothing to do with you. If you feel that you are sick and that you are a sinner, come to Me. You must know that you are great sinners.”

For this reason we must change our view. When we go to the homes of the brothers and sisters to preach the gospel, we should not judge the saints. We should not measure the heart or the appearance of the saints to determine whether their household is qualified to preach the gospel. We must believe that when the gospel is preached in their home, their household will change. The New Testament shows that the gospel was preached in the homes of sinners and in the homes of God-fearing people. Even though Zaccheus was a sinner, because he was a chief tax collector, the Lord Jesus said, “Zaccheus, hurry and come down, for today I must stay in your house...Today salvation has come to this house” (Luke 19:5, 9). Cornelius, a God-fearing man who gave many alms to the poor and frequently prayed to God, invited Peter to his home to preach the gospel to his friends and relatives (Acts 10:1-8, 24-43). We must go to both kinds of households.

We must do whatever we can so that open homes for the gospel is a universal practice. It does not matter whether a person is experienced; as long as he is saved, he should open his home for the preaching of the gospel. We are calling out to the saints, and we want every household to answer this call. Everyone, the old and the young, must preach the gospel. Let us put this to practice. When we preach the gospel, we should not worry about how to preach. We simply need to bear the responsibility of opening our homes and inviting our relatives, neighbors, and friends. We must also prepare some snacks; occasionally, we can even have a love feast. However, it is better to keep things simple and inexpensive. When the saints come together, they must practice speaking for the Lord by giving testimonies of how they were saved. The gospel meetings in the homes must not be turned into worship services.

Because believers in Christianity follow the customs of the nations, they cannot avoid the rituals in worship services. However, according to the record in the Scriptures, the Lord Jesus never used rituals for worship when He was in someone’s home, yet people were always willing to repent and receive Him. This is the true worship sought by the Father. True worship is not prostrating oneself on the ground. John 4 reveals that the true worshippers of the Father are those who drink the living water (vv. 14, 23-24). Luke 15 records the return of the prodigal son. The father saw the prodigal son from afar and ran to meet him, kissed him, and ordered the servants to put the best robe, a ring, and sandals on him. Then they slaughtered the fattened calf and called everyone to eat and rejoice together (vv. 11-24). When the son enjoyed what the father prepared, the father was worshipped. In the same way, the Lord does not want us to bow before Him; His delight is that we eat Him and receive Him. Hence, true worship is to use our spirit to receive the Lord as life, to eat the bread of life, and to drink the water of life.

In the past many Christians thought that breaking bread to remember the Lord was to meditate quietly upon all that the Lord passed through. I also practiced this for many years. I finally gained a true understanding of what the bread-breaking meeting on the Lord’s Day is supposed to be when I left mainland China. Then I wrote How to Break Bread. When the Lord established His feast, He took the bread and blessed it. Then He broke it and gave it to His disciples, saying, “Take, eat; this is My body.” Then He said, “Do this in remembrance of Me” (Matt. 26:26; Luke 22:19). What the Lord wants us to do is to eat. Eating is the true remembrance of the Lord. Hence, to remember the Lord we must know that He is the bread of life and then take and eat Him in true remembrance of Him. Before I had this realization, I used to pay much attention to kneeling in prayer; after I had this realization, I began to pay attention to whether or not my spirit was open and exercised and to whether or not I had touched the Lord. There should be no outward rituals in remembering the Lord. According to the Bible, we should return to our spirit. Everything depends on the spirit, not on letters.

In promoting the home gospel meetings, we do not want to give the saints a natural understanding or a religious concept. We must throw these things away. As long as a saint has a home, that home should be open for the gospel. Everyone should give his or her testimony and speak concerning the Lord Jesus. We should not speak too long; we should give a short word concerning our salvation. In this way, we will gradually produce many more saints who are able to preach the gospel. Preaching the gospel in the homes is a fountainhead from which we can draw much water. As long as we dig the well deep, the number of people who get saved in the homes will constantly increase.

CHAPTER TWELVE

THE FOUNDATION FOR THE SPREAD
OF THE LORD’S RECOVERY

EVERYONE BEING MOBILIZED TO PREACH THE GOSPEL

For many years the number of saints meeting regularly in the church in Taipei has been around four to five thousand. The spiritual life of the saints has been maintained through their meeting regularly, and they have grown in life. This is a positive situation. Many brothers and sisters are growing, and many new brothers and sisters are being brought into the church life. However, it is time for us to change from merely maintaining our situation to taking action. The church in Taipei must rise up. Even though four to five thousand is not a large number, if the saints rise up to move corporately, it will be significant and profitable, and we will be able to accomplish something.

According to the present strength of our meetings, it should not be a problem to increase our numbers. It should be easy to double our numbers by next year, and we should also be able to quadruple them. I say this because at least three thousand five hundred saints stood up in the meeting to express their desire to bring one person to the Lord every year. This means that next year we can add a minimum of three thousand five hundred new ones. If every saint brings at least one person to the Lord in the next year, we will double our numbers. In addition to this, we should strengthen the preaching of the gospel in our homes and among the students. By adding these two aspects, we should be able to quadruple our numbers next year. If we want to gain people, we all, including the older and the younger saints, must rise up and coordinate together. The Lord’s leading is for everyone to be mobilized as a soldier and to carry out his or her function.

THE FOCUS OF OUR WORK BEING
BEGETTING, NOURISHING, TEACHING,
AND ADMINISTRATING

In this message we will emphasize three matters: truth, life, and the church. With respect to the gospel, as long as we all preach the gospel, we will have good results. It is not difficult to beget children, but nourishing the children is not so easy. Teaching or educating children is even harder, because we must be educated first. We encourage all the saints in the Lord’s recovery to beget children; it is good to have many new ones. However, after children are born, we cannot discard them on the side of the road, nor can we abandon them in a nursery school. We must raise them up by nourishing them and giving them an education. Furthermore, we must bring them to the proper path. If we beget five thousand children next year, it will be a huge problem to nourish and educate them. How can we teach them if we are uneducated? In ancient China it was rare for women to receive an education. After they were married, they stayed at home to raise children. Even though the children received their mother’s love, they did not receive any education from their mother, because their mother was not educated.

In contrast to the situation in ancient Chinese households, the situation in Taiwan today is quite different. Nearly all young females receive a good education, one that is not inferior to the education received by males. Most young women today have graduated from high school. Therefore, they can bear the responsibility to both nourish and teach their children.

In order to keep the children whom we beget through preaching the gospel, we must educate them. Many do not know much about God, Christ, or redemption. We should know how to teach them these matters, because we have been taught the truth for many years. Not only do we have to beget, nourish, and teach; we also have to administrate. After we beget someone, we need to nourish and teach him. We must also lead him to participate in the proper church life and to function with the saints in the church. Then he will also be able to beget, nourish, teach, and administrate, and we will be able to continue to gain new ones. For this reason, we must learn how to beget, nourish, teach, and administrate.

When a couple gets married, they beget children. When the children are born, the couple will have no peace. Some people who get married today do not want to have children. This is not according to God’s will in His creation of man. Likewise, some Christians do not want to beget new ones. After being saved, they want to pray, fellowship with the Lord, read the Bible, and be spiritual. But they do not want to beget and nourish children. To them, begetting children is a suffering as well as a blessing. Some brothers refuse to be an elder or a deacon, one who takes care of the saints and bears responsibility in the church. They want only to be a simple Christian who is not bothered or troubled by anything. We cannot be like this. We must beget new ones, and we must nourish them. We cannot ask the elders to nourish our children, nor can we put our children in a nursery school. We must nourish them ourselves.

From our experience we know that begetting is easy, but nourishing, teaching, and administrating are not so easy. We have been begetting people for many years, but we lack adequate care and nourishment. It seems as though we either leave them at home, or we throw them out on the street. Some of our children die from the cold, some starve to death, and some are taken away by other people. Hence, we must change this situation. We must care for the people whom we beget through preaching the gospel, and we must nourish and teach them in order for them to be sustained. After teaching them, our care for them must be proper; we must bring them along the proper path, which is to live the proper church life and to function in the church. This must be the focus of our work.

PURSUING AND EXERCISING
IN TRUTH, LIFE, AND THE CHURCH

By the Lord’s mercy, I have been serving Him for more than fifty years. I have gained much experience during these years, but there are three items that are unresolved. First, how do we support the new believers so that we do not lose them after they are saved? Second, how should we cultivate them so that they will grow like young green sprouts? Third, how do we care for them? How do we care for a church when the number of saints increases from five thousand to ten thousand? It is simple to care for a small church with only thirty to fifty saints, but suppose the church in Taipei doubled its number from five thousand saints to ten thousand; how would we care for its administration? To support, cultivate, and administrate are three issues that need to be resolved.

If we follow the way of the world, we could support, cultivate, and administrate through organization, but the church is not an organization. We must therefore spend some time to consider these matters. According to our experience, supporting, cultivating, and administrating depend on all the saints. In other words, every brother and sister must exercise in the truth, in life, and in the church; then the new ones will spontaneously be supported, cultivated, and cared for. If we are unclear concerning the truth, do not have growth in life, and do not participate in the church life, the result of our leading people to be saved will be the abandonment of many babies along the roadside. When a family has a baby, the parents do not leave it for the grandmothers to raise. We cannot lead people to salvation and then rely on the full-timers or co-workers and elders to support, cultivate, and care for them. Even though children are burdensome and troublesome, God gave all mothers a particular love. If we can lead five people to salvation in a year, that is the Lord’s mercy; however, we must support them after they are saved. All mothers put their children first. Regardless of how busy a mother is, she will care for her children. Spiritually, this matter depends on our level of life. In order to resolve how to support, cultivate, and provide care, we must stop expecting others to take care of things for us; rather, we must do them ourselves. Therefore, we must know the truth, grow in life, and have a normal church life.

Laboring to Pursue the Truth

Most young women now receive a proper education. When they become mothers, they are able to educate their children. This principle also applies to us. We hope that all the brothers and sisters, including the co-workers and elders, would receive this word. We should not worry about how to support, cultivate, or administrate. Rather, we must pursue the truth, life, and the church. We need to labor in the truth; we should not be afraid of laboring on the truth. We must spend time in the truth. We should study the truth not only for the sake of our children but also for our own sake. Preaching the gospel requires labor—reading the Bible and studying the truth, including the Life-study messages. If a student does not labor, he will not get good grades at school.

In order to get into a good university, the young people in Taiwan all labor in their studies. Likewise, if we want to be useful in the Lord’s hands, we must labor when we read the Bible. We cannot read the Bible as if we are reading a newspaper or a novel. We must spend the time to labor in and research the Bible by getting into every word. We should even study the genealogy in the first seventeen verses of Matthew 1. When I was young, I studied the first seventeen verses of Matthew 1. Based on my study, in 1938 I wrote an article called “Gleanings from the Genealogy of Christ.” That article shows that I did a thorough study of the Lord’s genealogy. You too must put such labor into studying the Bible.

Exercising to Grow in Life

We must also grow in life. We should not be loose or indulge ourselves. Neither should we try to improve or reform ourselves. Self-improvement is of no use. We should always remember that we are not living for Jesus; we are living Christ. We must practice “not I, but Christ.” When something happens to us, we do not need to learn to be patient; instead, we should practice living in a way that “it is no longer I who live, but it is Christ who lives in me” (Gal. 2:20). We must exercise being rooted in Christ in all things (Eph. 3:17; Col. 2:7). This is to exercise in life. This is like playing the piano; if we skip one day of practice, our playing will not improve. We must exercise to live Christ. We should exercise to say, “I am a person in Christ; I must live in Christ, and I must be rooted in Christ.” It does not matter what kind of attitude others have toward us or in what way they speak to us, we should always be rooted in Christ. Such an exercise to be in Christ is to be “no longer I...but...Christ who lives in me.” We must exercise in this way every day so that we grow in life. Then after we lead people to salvation, we will spontaneously help them to live Christ.

For the building up of the church, we must not merely be zealous to preach the gospel; we must also have the truth, life, and the church as our foundation. We should study the truth diligently, just like a student studies algebra and geometry. Then our foundation will enable us to teach our children. Simply encouraging the saints is not enough to build up the church. All the brothers and sisters must be rooted in the truth and in life. We must hold fast to these three things: the truth, life, and the church; we cannot let them go. Even though we encourage the saints to be crazy and thick-skinned when they preach the gospel, their being so must be in the truth and in life; otherwise, there will be problems. We must watch to see that the saints are clear concerning the truth, that they are strong in life, and that they have a normal church life. We must care for these matters, pursue them, and exercise to be in them. This is the only way for the service in the church to be long-lasting and for the church to spread.

Having a Normal Church Life

We must also have a practical living in the church life. Even though the brothers are busy with their occupations and the sisters are busy with their households, we still must quietly consider how to properly apportion our time. Everyone should have a schedule in which we clearly list what we will do for the week. We are all busy, and we have many things that we must do; however, in order to learn to do things according to their importance and urgency, we should make a schedule. For example, when we receive a letter, we do not need to read it immediately if it is not urgent. Telegrams, however, are usually short and important and should be read immediately. Since we have so many things to take care of and not enough time for all of them, we must learn to take care of things in the order of their importance and urgency. Hence, we must make a schedule. Then we will know how much time we can spend daily laboring in the Lord’s Word.

For the church life, it is good for the saints to attend four meetings a week. In almost every place in the world, no one works on the Lord’s Day. Therefore, we should go to the Lord’s Day morning meeting and to the bread-breaking meeting in the evening. In addition, it should not be too difficult to have two evening meetings during the remaining six days in the week. It is necessary to have four meetings in the church life. We have considered combining the Lord’s Day morning meeting with the table meeting, but it is not so easy to combine them. If we are hasty, both meetings will suffer loss. To combine them in a good way, we must have the Lord’s Day meeting like some localities in America—they meet from the morning until about one or two in the afternoon. Then they stay and eat lunch together. In this way there is enough time for a message and to remember the Lord. They do this because it is not easy for the brothers and sisters who live far apart in large cities to make two trips to the meeting hall in one day. If the city is not large, and if the brothers and sisters do not live far apart from each other, it is better for them to meet in the morning and in the evening. In addition to the two Lord’s Day meetings, during the week there is the need for a prayer meeting and for a meeting to study the Bible. These four meetings are necessary.

No matter how busy they are, the saints must budget their time and endeavor to attend these four meetings. If we practice this, the ones under our care will gradually begin to do the same. We should not consider these four meetings to be insignificant; they have much influence on our living. Attending these four meetings can be compared to eating regular meals instead of starving oneself and then eating a huge meal. The church life is a healthy life; if we are so busy with other matters that we frequently miss the meetings and can attend the meetings only occasionally, it is like missing many meals and then eating a big meal sporadically. After a long period of time of eating in this way, we will not be very healthy.

In order to be clear about the truth, we must study the Bible every day. We should not read it in a general way; instead, we should study it. Merely reading the Bible every day is not enough. We should also use the best reference books so that our knowledge of the truth will constantly increase. By the Lord’s mercy I have not left His Word for the past sixty years. For this reason, the light within me is constantly increasing. The Lord’s Word has a free way to flow within me, and when it flows, the light comes from every side. This shows that we must know the truth.

In the future the full-time co-workers will encourage preaching the gospel on the campuses, in the homes, to the children, and in the community. Full-timers are needed for the gospel on the campuses and in the schools; otherwise, it will be difficult to maintain the gospel work. With regard to the children’s work, even though the junior high and high school students can teach in the children’s meetings, the children’s work will be carried forward by the full-timers, because they will prepare teaching materials and make a schedule. The number of children in the church in Taipei has dropped to five hundred because there is a lack of co-workers to carry the work forward. If the children’s work is to spread, we must preach the gospel. We should not limit our work to the children of the saints who are in our meetings; we also need to invite the children of our neighbors and friends. Furthermore, we hope that every home will be open for the gospel. This requires that the co-workers visit the saints in order to encourage them to open their homes and that the co-workers help the saints who are willing to open their homes to speak. Initially, the co-workers will have to take the lead in the homes, but after a few gospel times, the saints will be able to take care of the meeting. We need to be flexible in our practice. On the one hand, the co-workers need to go out and encourage the saints, and on the other hand, the saints should not depend on the elders and co-workers; they must learn to do things themselves.

If all the saints know the truth, have some growth in life, and live the normal church life, they will not be sidetracked or get into trouble regardless of how crazy they are when they preach the gospel or how thick their skin is. They will have the ground with people, and they will have the inward reality. When we learn the truth, have some growth in life, and participate in the proper church life, we spontaneously become stable and dependable people. We will regularly lead others to salvation, and they will do what we do. In this way, the church will be built up, and the Lord will have a testimony on the earth that will cause the bride to be prepared.

THE LORD TAKING THE WAY OF RECOVERY
FOR THE FULFILLMENT OF THE SCRIPTURES

You should never think that we are one of the many groups in Christianity. The leading that the Lord has given us is different from what is in Christianity; we are His recovery. Christianity lost this way more than one thousand years ago. The Lord wants us to take the way of recovery in order to fulfill the words He has spoken in the Scriptures. In the books of Galatians, Ephesians, Philippians, Colossians, and Romans, the Lord spoke many deep things, but we do not see much of the reality of these things. We should not think that it is impossible for these words to be fulfilled. We believe that the words in the Bible, regardless of how deep, high, or mysterious they are, will be fulfilled. If we are not willing to cooperate with the Lord to allow His words to be accomplished in us in this age, He will delay His return. To the Lord one thousand years are as a day; if He delays his coming for one thousand years, He will come one day later. The Lord has great patience, and He has endurance. The day will come when He will fulfill His word. May we be those who have received the grace and the blessing to allow the Lord to pass through us in this age so that His word can be accomplished and fulfilled.

God desires to gain a group of people who are clear concerning the truth and who have growth in life. He also desires to obtain the church life as the expression of the golden lampstand. We are preaching the gospel, speaking the truth, and leading people to salvation so that they may receive grace and enlightenment to be a part of the golden lampstand for the Lord’s testimony. We believe that this is what the Lord wants us to do, and we also believe that if we are faithful, the Lord’s grace will take us on in this way.

We truly are blessed people because the recovery is not what it was in the time of Martin Luther or what it was three hundred years ago or even what it was one hundred years ago. Every generation in the Lord’s recovery surpasses the generation preceding it. We hope that the younger generation will surpass us and will constantly follow the Lord and advance. Their ability to surpass us depends on the truth, life, the church life, and the gospel. Truth, life, and the church are the foundation, and the gospel is for spreading. It is only by having truth, life, and the church that we will be able to spread.

OUR EMPHASES IN THE CHURCH LIFE

There are a few more points for us to fellowship about. First, our feeling toward the church is very important. When we go out to preach the gospel, we should not think that we are great gospel preachers who can bring one hundred people to salvation. A believer with this attitude is finished; in other words, he has killed himself. We should not think that we are tremendous. It is the Lord’s mercy and grace if He uses us in any way. We must be humble and understand that everything we have is in the church and that the result of all our labor must be turned over to the church. Only the church can preserve us and balance us. As soon as we do not have the church life, we are on our own, and we are in danger. Moreover, if we do anything special on our own, we will wither, because it will result in division. There is only one Body of Christ, and there is only one way. Hence, we must lay a firm foundation in truth, life, and the church. The firmer the foundation is, the better. Then we will not suffer, nor will we be in any danger when we go out to preach the gospel, even if we lead tens of thousands of people to salvation.

Furthermore, we must always remember that there must not be parties in the church. Do not say that Apollos is higher than Paul or that Paul is deeper than Peter or even that Peter is older and more experienced. We must not make such distinctions. We must see that Paul is for us, Peter is for us, and Apollos is also for us. Paul said that all are ours (1 Cor. 3:22). We thank the Lord that He gave us Peter and Apollos and Paul; they are for us. If we say that we are following the way of Paul or that we belong to Peter or to Apollos, we have brought division into the church. This has been church history. We cannot afford to take that way.

BEING HUMBLE IN LEARNING FROM OTHERS,
IN NOT CRITICIZING OTHERS,
IN BEING HARMONIOUS IN ALL THINGS,
AND IN NOT CAUSING PROBLEMS

In the Lord’s recovery we must be humble in order to learn from others, to not criticize others, to be harmonious in all things, and to not cause problems. We must love all the churches and all the saints. We must continually maintain such an attitude. In the Lord’s recovery we are one, and everyone has his function. The elderly saints have their function, and the young saints have their function. We must thank the Lord that He gave us “Paul,” “Apollos,” and “Peter”; we must receive the supply from them. We absolutely cannot say, “I am for Paul,” or “I am for Peter.” We must not allow other saints to take sides with us. We must condemn any situation that results in the saints in a locality beginning to follow us.

We do not want people to follow us, nor do we want to follow men. Rather, we are for the Lord’s recovery, and we love the Lord’s recovery, all the churches, and all the brothers and sisters. We receive whoever can give us help, and we help whomever we are able to help. Wherever we go, we do not criticize, nor do we say, “This church is not as good as another local church.” We must not have such a thought. Some churches have more growth and others have less, but we should not discuss this. Our attitude must be that we are here to supply others with the Lord’s grace. We must also be humble, and we must receive the supply from others.

We must always be willing to learn no matter where we are. If there is something that can help us, we should learn from it. In the same manner, wherever we go, we must supply others and receive the supply from others. This is the way for everyone’s spirit to be in harmony. We cannot expect that every local church will have the same growth in life. This is impossible. We should not even have such an expectation. We must be one to harmoniously supply the saints wherever we are.

Moreover, we should not focus only on our own work. The Lord has given us a portion, which we must take care of, but we must not push others aside or trample on their portion. We must remember that the Lord has richly given every member to the church and that every member has the Lord’s riches. For example, even the little finger has its use. All the members have the riches of the Body. Hence, we must treasure all the brothers and sisters.

PRACTICING THE SMALL GROUPS TO GAIN PEOPLE
AND ALL THE MEMBERS BEARING THE BURDEN
OF SHEPHERDING AND TEACHING

If we want the church to continue to spread, every saint must pick up the responsibility to shepherd and teach. We will form small groups in every district, and every group will have twelve people, just as the Lord Jesus had twelve disciples. On the one hand, we will preach the gospel, and on the other hand, we will lead and perfect a few saints. When the number of saints in a group becomes too many, the group will split. This means that when those whom we have perfected learn how to lead others, they will go out to do the same things that we do. In this matter, we do not need to wait for the church to make arrangements. Instead, we should begin to take care of a few saints and gradually increase the number of those under our care. On the one hand, we will preach the gospel, and on the other hand, we will take care of the saints by feeding them as our spiritual children. The saints who have been under our care for one year will have some spontaneous growth.

The goal of leading people to salvation is to bring them into the church so that they will be established in the church. Hence, we need to support those whom we lead to salvation. If we do not support them, we will lead people to salvation with one hand and allow them to slip away through our other hand. We must avoid this. We should not bear children and then neglect to care for them. After we beget, we must feed our children and bring them into the church. Newly saved ones need to be led for some time before they will be stable in the church life. This is our goal.

CHAPTER THIRTEEN

THE WAY FOR THE CHURCHES
IN TAIWAN TO GO ON

(1)

Scripture Reading: Hab. 3:2; Ezek. 1:4

A TRUE REVIVAL

Hymn #212 in the Chinese hymnal was written after we had a thorough study of Ezekiel 1 more than twenty-three years ago. The messages given during those meetings were published in Chinese.

Ezekiel 1 speaks of a vision seen by Ezekiel in which a storm wind, coming from the north, brings a great cloud in which there is fire flashing. From the midst of the fire there is something like electrum in brightness (v. 4). This shows that in Ezekiel 1 there are four main items: the wind, the cloud, the fire, and the electrum. John Nelson Darby says that the electrum is “an unknown substance” that “some think a mixture of gold and silver.” According to the divine revelation, gold represents the manifestation of God’s divine nature. The storm wind comes from God, the cloud that comes with the wind contains a flashing sanctifying fire, and from the midst of the fire there is something like the glowing electrum, composed of the elements of gold and silver. This picture, which is full of spiritual significance, implies that every one of us must become a man of wind and cloud, filled inwardly with the divine fire, and full of the shining forth of the divine essence.

Five hundred years of Christian history have passed since Luther began the Reformation. The item most emphasized in Christianity during these years has been revival. According to church history, for the past five hundred years the Protestant churches have been maintained mainly by revival meetings. We cannot say that this is against the Bible; however, even with revival meetings the condition of Christian meetings has progressively declined, and the result is a loss of spiritual weight. When the gospel was preached in China, the Christians changed the word revival into excitement. This means that the meetings merely excited people. After a short time believers grew cold again, and they continued to live as they had in the past. For this reason, after the Lord raised up His recovery among us, we did not pay much attention to revival meetings; neither were we willing to use the term excitement meeting. There have been very few revival meetings among us.

I have been speaking God’s Word for many years, and I rarely quote the Minor Prophets in the Old Testament. However, for this meeting, there is one sentence that we can use: “O Jehovah, revive Your work / In the midst of the years” (Hab. 3:2). Hymns, #797 is also very appropriate, because the beginning of every stanza and the beginning of the chorus say, “Revive Thy work, O Lord!” However, in considering this matter, we will use hymn #212 in the Chinese hymnal.

If we read this hymn thoughtfully, we can see that the revival we are speaking of is not the shallow revival of which most of today’s Christianity speaks, much less is it a revival of excitement referred to by the Christians in China. The second half of the third stanza of hymn #212 says, “Burn out filthiness, / Burn up common things, / Making man correspond to God, / Holy without blemish.” The revival we are speaking of causes man to correspond to God by making man holy and without blemish. The second half of the fourth stanza says, “Divinity mingled with humanity, / Man’s spirit joined with God’s Spirit, / Causing God’s life / To be manifested in man.” This is the revival that we are referring to, and I believe this is also the revival that God desires. It is not an outward, so-called revival work, much less a revival of excitement; rather, it is “divinity mingled with humanity, / Man’s spirit joined with God’s Spirit, / Causing God’s life / To be manifested in man.”

In 1961 I conducted a Life-study of the book of Ezekiel, and I wrote this hymn. This proves that the revival that God showed us over two decades ago was a revival of “divinity mingled with humanity, man’s spirit joined with God’s Spirit, causing God’s life to be manifested in man.” This is also the revival that causes man to correspond to God. We need to sing these words until they enter into us and come out from us as a cry unto God: “Lord, bring in such a revival among us that makes man correspond to You so that Your life can be manifested in us.”

THE MODEL FOR THE ADMINISTRATION, MOVE,
AND BUILDING UP OF THE CHURCH

In the past few conference meetings more than six hundred saints have consecrated all their time for the Lord’s work and service, and another group of more than six hundred saints have consecrated themselves to be part-time for the Lord’s work and service. This will greatly expand and strengthen our service. We must, therefore, make new arrangements for the Lord’s work in Taiwan and for the building up of the church.

We will thoroughly fellowship with all the saints concerning the leading we have received from the Lord, the vision we have seen, and the way we must take in order to go on. We want every church and every saint in Taiwan to know how the work of the Lord’s testimony should go forward. We also want the churches to know how to build up the priesthood through service. We will fellowship as a family concerning the way we should move forward to promote the Lord’s testimony.

A REVIEW OF THE MOVE OF THE LORD’S RECOVERY

According to church history, the first meeting of the church was in Jerusalem. The church there was raised up and established by the apostles. From the beginning there was a large number of saved ones in that church. According to the record in Acts, one hundred twenty disciples prayed in one accord in the upper room for ten days. Then on the day of Pentecost the Holy Spirit was poured out, and three thousand people heard the gospel and were saved (1:13-14; 2:1-4, 41). When the first church was raised up, three thousand people were added to it on the first day. Not long after Pentecost, another five thousand men believed in the Lord on another day (4:4).

However, Acts does not say much about how the service in the early church in Jerusalem was carried out. The saints did not have their own meeting hall; they met in the temple and from house to house (2:46; 5:42). Verse 46 of chapter 2 says that all those who believed met from house to house. These words in Greek are specific. In the very beginning the church in Jerusalem had their meetings in the homes of the eight thousand saved ones; the saints met from house to house. This is what the book of Acts reveals.

The record in Acts does not show another church that had as many believers as the church in Jerusalem.
