Once we act, speak, and handle matters according to the position, name, and status of being elders, we fall into organization. We cannot serve the church based merely on the position and status of being elders; rather, we must serve by being in spirit and obeying the inner sense.

Being Young Sisters

A young sister who desires to serve the Lord full time might think that she should submit to elderly saints because she is a young sister. If her decision to submit is based on her youth and her gender, her submission is organizational. This sister should say, “Even though I am a sister, I am living in fellowship with the Lord. In this fellowship the Lord leads me step by step, and I am touching the anointing and acting according to the moving of the Spirit.” In this fellowship, there will be an organic submission that is not based on her age and gender but on the sense of life and the operation of the Spirit. This kind of obedience is not organizational; it is living and organic.

Cultivating Chinese Morality

Women in Chinese families were taught in former times to obey their fathers before marriage, to obey their husbands during marriage, and to obey their sons as widows. They were also taught the virtues of fidelity, charm, propriety in speech, and efficiency in needlework. These teachings relate to the organization of a family. These matters are good, and those who do not have the Lord Jesus are helped by them. We all need to maintain order in the country, to behave ourselves properly in society, and to be a decent and upright member in our family; however, these things are organizational. Therefore, in the church we do not talk about cultivating the self, putting the family in order, ruling the country, or living peacefully in the world. Instead, our focus is on exercising our spirit to walk according to the Spirit. Instead of being organizational, we should be organic. Those who are unsaved do not have the Lord, the Triune God, the divine dispensing, or the inward moving and anointing of the Spirit. Those who are saved have these items. We are different from the unbelievers in that we have the Triune God, who is the dispensing God, the anointing God, the operating God, and the sealing God. We have such a mysterious God in us.

The church is not an organization but a Body, an organism. Having the Triune God as our life is what makes this organism distinct. This is true in the church meetings, in our daily life, and in our family situations. When we love our wives, submit to our husbands, or take care of our children, it seems as if we are only cultivating ourselves and putting our family in order, but in fact, having received mercy from the Lord, we are following the inward operation of the Triune God. When a husband speaks to his wife, he should not have the thought, “Since I am the head, you must listen to me.” Such a thought is organizational. A husband should only have the feeling that the Triune God is in him and that he has to speak according to the operation of the Triune God. This is organic.

When we speak, every part of our body is active. This is organic. If we are organizational, our activities will be organized, and we will be an organization, an organized entity. We must learn to be organic in our service.

BEING ORGANIC, NOT ORGANIZATIONAL, IN SERVICE

Before a brother is appointed as an elder, he may have had no sense of being anything but a saint who simply served the church. After being asked to coordinate in the eldership, he may regard himself as an elder, and from that day forward, all his service may be based on an organizational understanding.

We need to ask ourselves whether our service comes out of an organizational or organic understanding. If a sister serves only because she has been given an “assignment” by the elders, her service is organizational. We have fellowshipped that it is difficult to appoint elders. Prior to being appointed to the eldership, a brother may be good, always exercising to be in spirit and organic. However, the moment he is asked to join the eldership, he becomes organizational. An organic brother can easily become an organizational elder. This principle is true not only in the church but even in the world. As soon as someone is assigned to be in charge or to take the lead, he undergoes a change in disposition and behavior. Prior to the assignment he had one disposition, but after the assignment he behaves organizationally based on his position. This is difficult to avoid.

We should not have group leaders and deputy group leaders, or responsible ones and coordinators, because as soon as there is such an arrangement, everything becomes organizational. In 1976 we built a huge meeting hall in Anaheim, California, that could seat four thousand people, but we did not have much arrangement for service related to the building. Taking advantage of this situation, a brother began to arrange service groups. Eventually, he built up a pyramidal organization. Initially, the brothers were organic, but soon everyone became organizational. One day I told the brothers in the elders’ meeting to abolish and tear down all the service groups. The elders asked, “How will the saints serve?” And I responded, “Whoever has the heart will come to serve; whoever does not have the heart will not serve.” After that, our service became living, and the number of serving ones was not reduced.

Fallen people are organizational by birth, and they form groups or communities, which are also organizations. However, the Bible shows that God does not want an organization; God wants an organism. Revelation speaks of the messengers of the churches. Anyone who is organic, in the spirit, and in life is a messenger of the church. We need to be clear that we should not serve organizationally; instead, we should serve organically. Our service is not organizational; it is organic. When this basic issue is resolved, it is easy to deal with other matters.

THE BODY OF CHRIST BEING ORGANIC,
NOT ORGANIZATIONAL

The Relationship between Apostles and Elders

Influenced by the Lord’s recovery, Christianity has begun to notice 1 Corinthians 12:28, which says, “God has placed some in the church: first apostles, second prophets, third teachers; then works of power, then gifts of healing, helps, administrations, various kinds of tongues.” I was born in Christianity. Since my youth I listened to preaching every Lord’s Day, but I had never heard a pastor speak of apostles, prophets, and teachers. It was not until the Lord’s recovery was raised up in China that Brother Nee took the lead to speak about these things and opened the door for us. Today in Christianity, especially in the East, people speak of apostles, prophets, and teachers, but they are not clear concerning what apostles, prophets, and teachers are. Even the saints among us are not clear, and some of our co-workers are not clear. What are apostles, prophets, and teachers? What are elders and full-time co-workers? What is the relationship between apostles and elders and between full-time co-workers and elders? The co-workers and elders need to be clear concerning these relationships.

The church in Jerusalem was the first church established on the earth. On the one hand, it was established by the Lord, and on the other hand, it was established by the first group of apostles through their preaching of the gospel. In Acts 2 Peter, standing with the eleven apostles, preached the gospel to the multitude, and about three thousand were saved. These three thousand new believers, in addition to the one hundred twenty disciples, became the church in Jerusalem (vv. 14-41; 1:15). Therefore, the first church was established by the twelve apostles. Although the Bible does not speak of the appointment of elders in Jerusalem, surely there were elders. Although it is not easy to see, the apostles who established the church in Jerusalem were the elders there, because it was through them that the three thousand were saved.

A large family may consist of multiple generations, including a grandfather, twelve sons, and the children of the twelve sons. When the grandfather dies, the twelve sons, that is, the second generation, become the elders. There is no need for them to be appointed, because it is clear to everyone in the family. Likewise, when the church was established at Pentecost, three thousand souls were saved, and afterward another five thousand were saved. There was no need to appoint elders, because it was obvious to all the believers that Peter and the other eleven apostles were the elders. In every family the children know who the father is.

Concerning the appointment of elders, the Bible does not say that elders were appointed in the church in Jerusalem. The elders were produced spontaneously, and they were the twelve apostles. Like the father in a family, they did not need to be appointed. The Bible first speaks of the appointment of elders in Acts 14:21-23, where Paul and Barnabas appointed elders in the churches in Lystra, Iconium, and Antioch. When Paul and Barnabas first passed through these places, they preached the gospel and raised up churches. After less than a year, they returned to appoint elders in every church.

Elders were appointed in every place where there was a group of believers meeting together as the church. Even though the believers were young, they were the church. Paul and his co-workers could not remain in these places to care for the churches; they had to leave. Consequently, there was a need for some to take care of the local affairs, so it was necessary to appoint elders in the churches that had been established for less than one year. Hence, the elders appointed could not have been very mature. They must have been considered as elders because they were a little more mature than the other believers in their locality. In order to avoid confusion, the apostles appointed elders in the churches, even elders who were not very mature or experienced. They were appointed elders because they were more mature compared to the other saints.

Concerning Young Full-timers

In his second ministry journey, Paul went to Lystra, and the church recommended a young man named Timothy (16:1-2). Timothy can be considered the first young full-timer among Paul’s co-workers. He was not brought up by Paul; instead, he was brought up and recommended to Paul by a local church. In 1 Timothy Paul said to him, “Do not neglect the gift which is in you, which was given to you by means of prophecy with the laying on of the hands of the presbytery” (4:14). The presbytery in this verse refers to the elders in Lystra who were only relatively mature. Paul did not lay hands on Timothy by himself; he did this together with the local elders in Lystra. Based on their laying on of hands, Timothy was under the elders. Notwithstanding this, Paul later charged Timothy to appoint elders. Initially, Timothy, a full-timer, was like an apprentice under the elders. After a period of time, he became an apostle and was qualified to appoint elders. When he began to serve full time, his service was based on the laying on of the hands of the elders. But at a certain time he had the maturity to appoint elders and could lay hands on the elders (5:22). Even an accusation from two or three witnesses against an elder could be presented to Timothy (v. 19). This means that a charge against an elder was brought to Timothy. Paul also told Timothy that when an elder sinned, he should reprove the elder before all, not privately (v. 20). Paul did not play politics. If a rebuke was needed, Paul indicated that it should be done publicly. This is different from our present practice. Paul’s practice was to publicly rebuke any elder who sinned so that other elders might hear and be warned. Regrettably, such practices have been replaced by a willingness to be political. We play politics, but Paul did not.

Raising Up Prophets and Teachers

In the local church in Antioch there were prophets and teachers who were raised up by the Holy Spirit (Acts 13:1-2). Barnabas was a Levite (4:36). He belonged to the priestly tribe, and he was raised up by the Holy Spirit after his salvation. Acts 13 says that Barnabas was one of the prophets and teachers in Antioch. It is difficult for us to determine whether he was a prophet or a teacher. However, whether he was a prophet or a teacher, he was not appointed by men; he was raised up by the Holy Spirit. Saul of Tarsus, who once opposed the churches, was among these prophets and teachers. After he was gained by the Lord, his whole being was revolutionized, and he began to preach the Lord Jesus. Even though the disciples were fearful of Paul, Barnabas contacted him, served with him in the work, and ministered together with him. Thus, Paul became one of the prophets and teachers in Antioch. Both Barnabas and Paul were not appointed by men. This is strong proof that prophets and teachers are not appointed by men. They are not like today’s pastors who need to be ordained by human hands.

The prophets and teachers in Acts 13 were appointed by the Holy Spirit. We do not know when they were appointed by the Holy Spirit. The Bible says only that there were prophets and teachers in the church life in Antioch. As they were ministering to the Lord, the Holy Spirit said, “Set apart for Me now Barnabas and Saul for the work to which I have called them” (v. 2). The moment they set out for the ministry, they became apostles. Even as apostles, they were not sent out by men but were appointed by the Holy Spirit to preach the gospel. The result of their gospel preaching was the raising up of local churches. Afterward, they appointed elders in the churches.

After churches came into existence and elders were appointed, young people who loved the Lord and desired to serve Him full time were raised up in these localities. Timothy is an example. After the church in Lystra was raised up, the local elders laid hands on a young full-timer named Timothy. After he participated in the work and gained experience, he was charged to appoint elders by the laying on of his hands. If an elder in a locality sinned, the witnesses could go to Timothy to present their accusation against the sinning elder.

THE HOLY SPIRIT’S ORGANIC ACTIONS

The record in the Bible does not reveal the development of an organization. Acts 13 clearly says, “The Holy Spirit said, Set apart for Me...They then, having been sent out by the Holy Spirit...” (vv. 2, 4). This shows that the setting apart and the sending out of the apostles was organic. Furthermore, Paul appointed elders in every city. This seems to be organizational, but in 20:28 Paul said, “Take heed to yourselves and to all the flock, among whom the Holy Spirit has placed you as overseers.” This shows that the appointment of the elders was by the Holy Spirit. It was the Holy Spirit who appointed the elders to be overseers of the flock to shepherd the church of God. In chapter 14 Paul appointed elders in every church (v. 23), but in chapter 20 he said that the Holy Spirit appointed the elders. This proves that when Paul appointed the elders, he was in spirit. Therefore, he was able to say that his action was the action of the Holy Spirit. Paul did not say that he had the position to appoint elders as an apostle sent by the Lord. If this was the case, the elders he appointed would not have been the elders the Holy Spirit appointed.

Concerning the appointment of elders, we should be able to say with confidence that the elders we appoint are elders appointed by the Holy Spirit. In 2 Timothy 1:6 Paul referred to his laying on of hands, saying, “Fan into flame the gift of God, which is in you through the laying on of my hands.” Timothy needed to fan into flame the gift he received through the laying on of Paul’s hands. When the elders and Paul laid hands on Timothy, a gift was bestowed on him. This indicates that the laying on of hands was the operation of the Holy Spirit. In other words, the laying on of hands by the presbytery and Paul was organic, not organizational. It was an organic action of the Body of Christ. Therefore, a spiritual gift was transmitted from the Body of Christ into Timothy. This proves that this action was not organizational; it was absolutely organic.

Timothy was a young person, yet Paul charged him, saying, “Let no one despise your youth” (1 Tim. 4:12). Timothy was a young apostle, but he could appoint elders, reprove elders, and even remove someone from the eldership. Paul encouraged Timothy not to be timid, because God had not given Timothy a spirit of cowardice but of power, love, and sobermindedness (2 Tim. 1:7). Paul also charged him to fan that gift into flame (v. 6). All the charges in Paul’s Epistles to Timothy were based upon this gift. The gift in Timothy’s spirit was not a gift of cowardice, but it needed to be fanned into flame. Therefore, Timothy did not carry out the charges in these Epistles by his own effort but by the gift that was fanned into flame, that is, by his burning spirit. His actions were not organizational; they were organic.

Paul also said that Timothy should know how to conduct himself in the house of God based on the Epistles Paul had written (1 Tim. 3:15). Just as Timothy received this word from Paul, the elders need to receive this word so that we may know how to conduct ourselves in the house of God, which is the church of the living God. In the house of God, the church of the living God, we cannot be organizational. We can only be organic. The house of God is the church of the living God; it is the pillar and base of the truth. The house of God is also the great mystery of godliness—God manifested in the flesh (vv. 15-16). This house is God manifested in the flesh. Our activities in the house of God must not be according to organization. Instead, everything we do in the house of God must be organic; it must be according to the mysterious manifestation of God in the flesh. This is not organizational; it is organic.

We truly hope that while leading the churches, the elders in all the localities would not forget that we are in the house of the living God. We are not in an organization, not in the denominations, much less in a social organization. We are in the house of the living God, which is the manifestation of God in the flesh. Hence, when we serve as elders, all our actions and decisions must be the manifestation of the living God—they must be organic. We all should have this basic knowledge. According to history, the apostle joined the presbytery to lay hands on a young full-timer. Later, this young full-timer could appoint elders, reprove elders, and remove someone from the eldership. All these matters were not done organizationally. They were organic.

OVERTHROWING THE CONCEPT OF ORGANIZATION

Now we will consider the practical application of our fellowship. Who should the young full-time serving ones listen to in their service? Suppose that in a local church there are some co-workers and many young full-time serving ones. Who should the young ones listen to? This question is difficult to answer, because often both the elders and the co-workers have laid hands on them. This is also difficult because even though the full-timers were under the elders who laid hands on them, they may later be charged to appoint elders. God has no thought of organization. The elders laid hands on Timothy, but even when Timothy was young, Paul exhorted him to not let anyone despise his youth, and Paul also charged him to lay hands on the elders. Shortly after the elders laid hands on him, Timothy was qualified to lay hands on the elders. With just this one example, God completely demolished the concept of organization.

The elders laid hands on Timothy, but soon after that Timothy was charged to lay hands on the elders. This is anti-organization. Timothy was probably saved through the elders’ preaching of the gospel, and he was probably baptized by the elders. It was also the elders who commended Timothy to Paul and laid hands on him together with Paul. Thus, if the church and the work were based on the concept of organization, the elders would be his seniors, and he would be their junior. But the Lord has overthrown organization. The elders who laid hands on Timothy were not qualified to appoint elders; instead, Timothy, who received the elders’ laying on of hands, was qualified to appoint elders. When an elder sinned, Timothy even had the position and qualification to receive an accusation against the elder from two or three witnesses (5:19). Suppose the sinning elder was the one who preached the gospel to Timothy, led him to be saved, baptized him, commended him to Paul, and laid hands on him. The elder could say that he was above Timothy and that Timothy was beneath him. This is an organizational concept. It is organizational to consider oneself the patron of a serving one. God’s ways are particular. He terminates all organizational concepts and practices.

The Body of Christ is not organizational; it is organic. Timothy was not raised up by Paul. Rather, he was raised up by the church in Lystra and then recommended to Paul. This was an organic procedure. Paul did not receive Timothy according to organization. Paul, together with the elders, laid hands on Timothy. The laying on of hands was not organizational; it was organic. When Paul laid hands on others, it was according to the operation of the Holy Spirit. When he and the elders laid hands on others, it was an action of the Body. Therefore, there was a flow in the Body that flowed into this full-timer and became a gift within him. These matters were organic, not organizational. Many ordinations are organizational. People are given a position and a name without the organic operation of the Spirit, but the laying on of hands in the Body of Christ is an organic operation.

The laying on of hands by Paul and the elders was an action of the Body. In the Body the Holy Spirit operates in newly consecrated full-timers to constitute them as gifts. When this gift was manifested in Timothy, he appointed elders and laid hands on them according to his organic function. It was not because of his position that two or three witnesses could bring an accusation against an elder to Timothy; it was because of his organic function. Timothy received the laying on of hands from the elders according to the organic function of the Body; likewise, he appointed elders and laid hands on them according to the same organic function. It was in this same organic function in the Body that he could rebuke a sinning elder. All these matters are organic; they are not organizational.

This should be our practice today. The young full-timers that are raised up in the church in Taichung do not need to be approved by the brothers in Taipei. Rather, the brothers in Taichung, as members of the Body of Christ, can consider, through the operation of the Spirit, whether the saints are suitable to serve full time. This is an organic matter; it is not organizational. Whether or not this matter is organic depends on the way the elders handle it. If they stand merely in the position as elders, their action will be organizational. If they live and act as organic members of the Body by exercising their spirit to contact the saints and minister life to them, their action will be organic. Having been raised up in a church and also considered and confirmed by the elders in that church, the full-timers should be willing to submit themselves to the elders. However, when making arrangements concerning the full-timers, the elders should not stand merely in a position as elders and make arrangements; rather, they should exercise their organic function in the Body. Furthermore, the serving ones should listen to the elders but not merely because they are young. Otherwise, their submission will be organizational. Both the serving ones and the elders need to serve together in the church in life and under the anointing.

THE LORD’S RECOVERY TAKING THE WAY
OF THE ORGANIC BODY

Christianity today is deformed and organizational. It forms committees to prepare budgets and raise funds to hire workers. If they cannot hire people who are trained, they send young people to seminaries for training and then assign work to them. We cannot take this way. We are the Lord’s recovery. The Lord’s recovery is to recover the Body of Christ; it is to recover an organism, not an organization. We have many co-workers and churches, and young people are being raised up to serve the Lord full time. We have the resources, but we should not take the way of organization, that is, the way of a corporation. We should take the organic way, the way of the Body. If we take the way of a corporation, we will become a denomination. This crucial matter must be clearly presented to the brothers and sisters. We must not go backward; we have only one way—the way of the organic Body. We must advance boldly.

Being organic depends mainly on the elders. The elders must forget that they are elders in their actions, intentions, and concepts. The elders are not bureaucrats holding official posts. The elders exist because there is the need for arrangement in the church services to avoid confusion. The elders should not replace the prophets or the teachers. The eldership does not involve rank; it involves only responsibility. Therefore, we should not turn the function of an elder into a mere title. An elder is a steward who takes care of the affairs of the church. For example, the elders make arrangements for different kinds of meetings, including schedules and how to lead the saints in the meetings. The Bible clearly says that the elders should not lord it over others but should be patterns of the flock (1 Pet. 5:3). The elders should forget position and status. They should not call themselves elders. They should only be patterns of the flock. In this way we will not repeat the mistakes of Christianity, nor will we take the way of organization. Rather, we will let the Holy Spirit have the ground in us to raise up our organic function.

In addition, the young full-timers should learn the proper way to coordinate in the church. Their submission should involve an organic operation that is much more than their human submission to parents or teachers. This is possible because the Triune God is in us. He is our life and our Lord. He is living. He can be our moment-by-moment, inward leading. We should exercise to live in the Lord. Then instead of being in a religious organization, we will be living members of the living Body of Christ. In this way our actions will be organic functions. Otherwise, we will be merely organizational. We should all be living members of an organism. All our walk and actions should issue from organic functions.

BEING ONE SPIRIT WITH THE LORD
AND CARRYING OUT
THE ORGANIC FUNCTION OF THE BODY

In 1 Corinthians 7:12 Paul said, “To the rest I say, I, not the Lord.” Paul boldly declared that his words in verse 12 were not the Lord’s speaking. Is his declaration organic or organizational? According to organizational thinking, the Corinthian believers could have told Paul not to speak until Christ, the Head, spoke. Since our knowledge concerning service may not be thorough, we may have concepts that we think are spiritual but are actually organizational. For example, we may say that it is organizational to do something that the Lord has not told us to do. We often say that we should not take any action until we have prayed and fellowshipped thoroughly. However, it seems that in 1 Corinthians 7 Paul had not prayed thoroughly, because it was he, not the Lord, who was speaking. Here, we have to change our concept. Paul was not as spiritual as we are, nor did he pretend to be spiritual. He clearly indicated that it was he, not the Lord, who was speaking. Then in verse 25, concerning virgins, he said, “I have no commandment of the Lord, but I give my opinion as one who has been shown mercy by the Lord to be faithful.” Our opinions are destructive, yet Paul gave his opinion without the Lord’s commandment. If I said, “Brothers, I have no commandment of the Lord, but I give my opinion,” I am afraid that everyone would disagree with me.

In 1 Corinthians 7:40 Paul said, “According to my opinion; but I think that I also have the Spirit of God.” This is marvelous. It does not seem logical that Paul could have the Spirit of God without the Lord speaking. However, the significance of Paul’s word is that we should not be organizational, nor should we say, “I am doing this because the Lord said so.” Paul spoke, but not the Lord. Paul did not have the Lord’s commandment, but he gave his opinion. Paul could do this because he had the Spirit of God. As a person who was one spirit with the Lord, his walk was in spirit. Since he walked in spirit, he disregarded organizational position and religious concepts. He was joined to the Lord as one, and his speaking and acting were organic functions of the Body. Paul did not have any position, nor did he act according to religious teachings. Rather, he was joined to the Lord as one spirit and therefore had an organic function in the Body.

We need to have a deeper knowledge concerning spiritual matters. Christianity teaches people merely to keep a position and obey orders; hence, it is organizational. When I speak, my whole body moves. No member of my body has the concept or thought of keeping a position or obeying commands. The move of my body is organic. After this fellowship, we should be clear that our service is not a matter of keeping a position or obeying commands. Our service is a matter of having the Spirit of God, the Spirit of the Lord; this is to be like Paul, who said, “I think that I also have the Spirit of God.” If we are one spirit with the Lord, instead of keeping a position or merely obeying commands, we will exercise our organic function. If we are clear concerning this, we will be greatly blessed and not have any problems. At the same time, we will know our position in the Body. We will know to whom we should listen; that is, we will listen to the organic function of the Body, and our living will be in the Body.

CHAPTER EIGHTEEN

THE ORGANIC FUNCTION
OF THE BODY OF CHRIST

(2)

THE ORGANIC FUNCTION OF THE BODY

All activities in human society are organized. For example, among human beings, the cultivation of young people requires organization. In the church, however, how should we produce workers to meet the need of spreading? Paul and Timothy are good examples. We will not use Peter as an example, because he was appointed by the Lord Jesus while the Lord was in the flesh. Since we do not have the Lord’s physical presence with us today, we cannot take Peter’s experience as an example. The Bible shows that after the Lord Jesus appointed the twelve apostles while He was in the flesh, He appointed Barnabas and Paul according to His invisible presence and in His status as the ascended Head. Barnabas and Paul were appointed as apostles without any element of human work or organization. They were appointed by the organic operation of the Lord as the Spirit.

Paul was called when he met the Lord on the way to Damascus (Acts 9:1-6; 26:12-18). After his conversion he served the Lord fervently, and his function was manifested. The Lord told Paul only that he would be sent to the Gentiles. Besides this, the Lord did not tell him what to do. The Bible does not reveal how the Lord appointed Paul. The New Testament discloses very little about how the Lord’s workers were appointed or how they worked, because such a record would be used for organizational purposes.

After Paul met the Lord, he spontaneously and organically followed the Lord according to the divine life he had received from the Lord. When Ananias sought out Paul, he also was carrying out his organic function as a member of the Body of Christ and not because he was sent by men. He laid hands on Paul and told Paul what the Lord wanted him to do (9:10-19). When Paul went to Jerusalem, the disciples in Jerusalem were afraid to contact him because he had persecuted the church. Eventually, Barnabas contacted him. This contact came out of Barnabas’s exercise of his organic function in the Body, not from Peter’s instruction (vv. 20-28).

In Acts 9 Paul left Jerusalem and returned to Tarsus. In chapter 11 some of the disciples from Jerusalem, who were scattered abroad, went forth proclaiming the gospel, reaching as far as Antioch. Believers were raised up in places even among the Gentiles. Barnabas, according to his organic function in the Body, was sent from Jerusalem to visit the believers as far as Antioch. After visiting the believers, Barnabas went forth to Tarsus, found Paul, and brought him to Antioch, where he and Paul remained. In chapter 13 Paul was one of the prophets and teachers in the church in Antioch. Paul may have been perfected through Barnabas, since it was Barnabas who brought Paul into the Lord’s work.

Acts 13 shows that in the church in Antioch there were five prophets and teachers, the first being Barnabas and the last Paul. There is no mention of elders and deacons. As the prophets and teachers were ministering to the Lord, the Holy Spirit said that Barnabas and Paul should be set apart and sent out to do the Lord’s work (v. 2). This was the Holy Spirit’s operation. The Bible refers to Barnabas and Paul as apostles when they were sent out (14:4, 14). Their first journey ended in chapter 14 when they returned to Antioch (v. 26). In his second journey Paul went to Lystra, and there he met Timothy (16:1).

The church in Lystra was established by Paul in his first journey, and elders were appointed there within a short time (14:6-7, 21-23). Not long afterward Paul passed through again, and the brothers commended Timothy to him. According to the Epistles to Timothy, Paul and the elders in Lystra laid hands on Timothy (1 Tim. 4:14; 2 Tim. 1:6). Timothy was a young full-timer who had a desire to serve God. He was raised up by a local church, and he was recommended to the apostle by the elders. Their laying on of hands was not an ordination; to be ordained is organizational. The laying on of hands indicates identification and fellowship, in which the Spirit of life is imparted for the purpose of bestowing a spiritual gift.

Timothy’s spiritual gift was not manifest at the beginning of his service. In Acts 17 Timothy’s function was manifested while they were in Greece. Paul mentioned Silvanus, Silas, and Timothy as his co-workers when he wrote his first Epistle to the Thessalonians (1:1; Acts 18:1, 5; 2 Cor. 1:19). In 1 Thessalonians Paul says that they were apostles (2:6). In Acts 16 Timothy was still young, but in chapter 18 he was considered to be an apostle. In 1 Timothy 5:19 Paul indicates that an accusation against an elder could be submitted to Timothy, which means that he was able to properly respond to accusations against elders. Surely this shows that the young Timothy had been perfected to be an apostle.

PERFECTING THE YOUNG PEOPLE
TO TAKE THE BODY AS THEIR PROTECTION

We have many young people who have a desire to serve full time. The way for us to perfect them is to hand them over to the Body, just as Timothy was handed over to the Body. Then the church in Lystra recommended Timothy and handed him over to the apostle. The way to perfect is clearly presented: the apostle with the elders and the elders in coordination with the apostle were responsible for his perfection. Perfection is by the Body. The Body perfects the young people, and the Body becomes their protection.

The church in Lystra commended Timothy to Paul. Then the elders and Paul laid hands on Timothy, thereby placing him under the care of the church, under the elders. Without the function of the elders, Timothy would not have been fully attached to the Body. Even if Paul had been able to provide him with some perfection by himself, Timothy could have had an improper attitude toward the church and the elders. This shows God’s wisdom and the work of the Holy Spirit. Paul did not lay hands on Timothy by himself. If he had done this, his actions would not have been according to the principle of the Body. Rather, he laid hands on Timothy together with the elders of the church. This shows that Timothy was perfected by the apostle with the church and by the church in coordination with the apostle. After Timothy was perfected, he was able to lay hands on others and even to respond properly to accusations against elders. However, he was not proud toward the elders and the church, because the elders had laid hands on him. Such a relationship is crucial.

LEARNING FROM OUR HISTORY

I went to Shanghai in 1946. At the end of the year I moved there and began coordinating with the brothers in the work and in leading the church. At the time there was a group of students who were being perfected under my ministry. In 1949 I moved to Taiwan, and according to the arrangement in the work, this group of young people also came to Taiwan. I now regret that my perfecting work was not as complete as Paul’s perfecting work on Timothy. The young people were short of certain elements. The work committed them into my hands for their perfecting, so they came to Taiwan. I assigned three of them to be under the leading of the brothers in Kaohsiung. However, in less than a year the responsible brothers told me that they had no way to lead the young brothers, because they falsely claimed that they had been perfected by Brother Nee. This was not accurate. Brother Nee did not minister for six years, from 1942 to 1948, and the church in Shanghai was restored only after the surrender of Japan in 1946. At that time, we began with about a hundred saints. A year later we began the practice of the whole church preaching the gospel, and hundreds of people were baptized. By the summer of 1947 the church in Shanghai held the bread-breaking meeting in seventeen districts. Therefore, these young people were actually under my perfection.

The church in Shanghai experienced a revival in the spring of 1948. Responsible brothers from the north, the northeast, the interior provinces as far as Hankow, and from the south as far as Kwangchow (Canton) wanted to come to Shanghai to see the revival. However, Brother Nee had not yet resumed his ministry; he was still in Foochow. Therefore, I went to Foochow to help with the resumption of his ministry, and I also accompanied him to Shanghai. In the resumption meetings we enjoyed the Lord’s presence. Therefore, Brother Nee decided that those who were present in the meetings should go to Kuling to be in his training, and that I should remain in Shanghai to lead the church. The next year, 1949, the civil war within China became critical, and government agencies were moved from Shanghai to Taiwan. I also came to Taiwan.

This history shows that the young brothers were not led by Brother Nee. Since they were not able to be perfected in the locality where they were, I brought them to Taipei and continued to lead and perfect them. However, I did not follow Paul’s example to coordinate with the elders in perfecting them, and they became detached from the church. Eventually, they left even though they were responsible for many service-related functions in the churches. As a result of their pride, they criticized the other co-workers, and we were unable to rescue them.

In 1954 and 1955 some brothers proposed that we invite Brother T. Austin-Sparks to come to Taiwan. He came in 1955 and again in 1957. After his second visit we had problems. As I look back, I see that the source of the problems was a lack in perfecting. This gave ground for pride to take root in those young brothers. Because they were not like Timothy, problems occurred. After Brother Sparks’s visit, they began to say that they had seen a glorious vision of the full Christ. This situation caused the greatest wounds in our history in Taiwan. To this day we can still see the tragic result of these divisions in the Body of Christ.

We must seriously consider the way to perfect the young people. If there are loopholes in our perfecting, problems will arise. This is similar to cultivating fruit trees in an orchard. If we do not properly cultivate the trees, there will be problems: bugs will eat the leaves and branches, and birds will eat the fruit. Therefore, we need to pay much attention to the perfecting of the young people. The young brothers and sisters have a great future, but if their perfecting is flawed, they will not be safeguarded and protected. If there are loopholes, disasters will be unavoidable. This will damage the future of their whole life.

Problems arose, and I warned the brothers that if they left, they would continually divide among themselves. More than twenty years have passed, and my word has proved true. Among those few brothers, no two are coordinating together; they are all separated from one another. They damaged the Body of Christ and created division. As a result, they are divided, and they are ruined. It is not that they did not have light or that they did not see the church. Their speaking concerning the ground of the church was clear. They know that there is only one Body and that there is only one church in the universe. They know that the expression of the church is in the principle of one church in one city. Today they are in America, but it has been difficult for them to preach the truth there. They may lead some students to salvation, but they cannot speak the truth concerning the church, because they do not have the proper standing.

This can be compared to the difficulty of divorced persons being reconciled with their former spouses. When these brothers were with us, they were “married” to the church, but now they are “divorced” from the church. By the Lord’s mercy, some are still willing to read our books; thus, they still have a way to receive some supply. In the early days they declared that they were helped by Brother Sparks to see and know the vision of the full Christ, but now they have nothing. It is a great mistake to be critical of others and to look down on others.

THE YOUNG SERVING ONES NEEDING
TO BE FEARFUL OF BEING PROUD

The future of the young serving ones is limitless. The Lord will give a considerable number of them important services in the carrying out of His commission. However, when they are given some responsibility, their pride will become a source of temptation. Thus, they should be fearful of their pride.

In 1950 Brother Nee went to Hong Kong and brought a revival to the church. He sent me a telegram asking me to come to Hong Kong and help lead the service of the church, including that of the elders, co-workers, and deacons. I was absent from one of the revival meetings, but during this meeting Brother Nee said, “Although Brother Lee has been used by the Lord, he is not proud.” Please forgive me for speaking about myself. Brother Nee spoke this word as a warning so that those who had handed themselves over to the Lord would have no expectation of a future for themselves. The Lord will have mercy on those who truly give themselves to Him, and He will perfect them to be useful. However, once a person becomes useful, it is easy for him to become proud. Pride is a worm that destroys us by devouring us from within.

The brothers who became a problem were not fearful of the element of their pride. When they were with us, they listened to me but despised the other co-workers. This is pride. In the future you may be supplied with a great measure of grace by the Lord, and He may perfect you in order to use you to a great extent. After accomplishing such a work, you should still go before the Lord and say, “I am an unprofitable slave; I have done what I ought to have done” (cf. Luke 17:10). Even if you have seen the vision of Christ, you should not think that others have not seen it. It is wrong to say that others have no vision. If you have seen a vision and know the Lord’s way, you will not intimidate others or promote yourself. Instead, you should walk quietly according to the Spirit and minister Christ in the meetings of the church in your locality.

If a brother is raised up in a local church, other churches will learn about him, even if he has a quiet manner. The churches will surely hear about him and welcome him. In this way he will be blessed, and the churches will also be blessed, supplied, and established through him. However, he should be fearful of becoming proud or of seeking a way to advance. The doors that the Lord wants to open will be automatically opened. May the Lord cover me with His precious blood. I have the position to speak such a word, because I am leading the churches, and I have never sought to advance myself. It was not my intention to work in the United States. In 1938 I received two checks: one check was for my traveling expenses to America, and the other was to cover one year’s expenses for my family. At that time I did not have the Lord’s leading to go to America. But twenty years later, in 1958, by the Lord’s sovereign arrangement I was invited to London and Denmark, and I passed through America.

If you have Christ and can minister Christ, you do not need to look for openings; doors will open for you. Joseph had an abundance of grain, so all the earth came to him to buy grain. All five continents are open to the testimony of the Lord’s recovery. My only concern is that we are not perfected. When we are perfected, we can be sent out. There are too many places in need of ones who can be sent. It would not be too much to send three or four hundred to South America. Many places in Europe are also waiting. We must always be afraid of arrogance and pride, especially if we have some spiritual constitution and gift. We must always remain in humility.

NOT FORMING PARTIES
WITHIN THE UNIQUE BODY OF CHRIST

I have often considered the incident with the brothers who stirred up the trouble in Taiwan, because it left a great wound. Not only did the brothers make the mistake of being proud, they also formed themselves into a party. They had no secrets among themselves, but they were tightlipped with the other co-workers. In the Body of Christ the members should not form parties. There cannot be a “small Body” within the Body. If there is a “small Body” within the Body, it will become a cancer. Eventually, the situation among those brothers became cancerous, and it devastated the Body of Christ.

Whether we are in Taichung, London, or Hong Kong, we should not try to gain some who would follow us. This is to form a small circle within the Body, and it is extremely dangerous. This is like two sisters who are willing to tell each other their secrets but who are unwilling to speak to their mother. Relationships like this need to be terminated. We are in one universal Body, and there should be no small circles within the one large circle of the Body. In the Body there is no such thing as one member being dearer or nearer to another member.

I began serving the Lord in Chefoo more than fifty years ago, but I do not have any co-workers with whom I have an intimate, personal relationship. Brother Chang has served with me for over fifty years, and Brother Liu has coordinated with me in the ministry of the word. Many saints probably think that these brothers are very dear to me. If you were to ask them, they would say that I have given them “hot and sour soup,” not “sweet soymilk.” It is the same in the United States; I do not have any co-workers with whom I am intimate on a personal level.

There are several co-workers who have left us. Some of them accused me of being wrong, while saying that they were right. It is strange that those who say that they are right often have the most difficulty working with others. But even though I am wrong, I have many co-workers. Nevertheless, I am not intimate with any of them. I do not give them “sweet soymilk” to drink; rather, I give everyone “hot and sour soup.” Those who are new full-timers should realize that I do not serve “sweet soymilk.”

ONE BODY, ONE WORK, AND ONE WAY OF RECOVERY

The church is the Body of Christ, and the Body is uniquely one. The Lord desires to recover this one Body. You should not think that I control people or try to wield power over the whole earth. When we were in Shanghai and Brother Nee was leading the church, some gifted ones came into our midst. They could preach the gospel and work, and they knew that the way of the Lord’s recovery was right. However, in their view, this “territory” was “occupied” by Brother Nee, and so by remaining in the recovery, they would have no way to gain their own territory. Eventually, they left the recovery, and some of them became famous preachers. Many of the Chinese evangelists who are now famous were among us at one time. Some formed their own groups, others established their own work, and still others gained honorary doctorate degrees. They knew that this was the Lord’s unique way, but they wanted their own work.

There is only one way, one Body, and one recovery of the Lord. When Brother Nee was raised up, he pioneered the way, and it was difficult. We are his successors. By the Lord’s grace I can say that when Brother Nee was taking the lead, I was submissive and did not dissent. Although he and I were only two years apart, I never had an opinion about him. I never dissented in the co-workers’ meetings. In the work of the ministry, I did whatever I was asked to do; I had no opinion. I have often said that I can submit to any person because I can submit to one person. Brother Nee showed me the way of the recovery, and for this reason I submitted to him.

In 1934 Brother Nee was going to be married in Hangchow, and he asked me to be his best man. The marriage stirred up a great turmoil for him. When he came to Shanghai, we met, and I tried to comfort him, saying, “Brother Nee, there is no natural friendship between us. I am taking this way because you have led me to see that this is the Lord’s way. Please be at peace, even if you give up this way, I will still take this way. I am taking this way not because there is a relationship between us, but because I have seen that this is the Lord’s way. Even if you give it up, I will still take it.” I hope the young brothers and sisters would see this way and would be able to say to me, “Brother Lee, you have led us to take this way, but we want to tell you that even if you give it up, we will still take it.”

Our God is uniquely one, and all the things in the universe created by Him are one in substance. Likewise, everything related to the church is intrinsically one. Ephesians 4:4-6 speaks of one Body, one Spirit, one hope, one Lord, one faith, one baptism, and one God and Father of all. Christianity is in a situation of apostasy because its numerous divisions deny this oneness. However, the Lord’s church is essentially one. We are here to bear the testimony of oneness. We need to see that the Lord’s church is one, the Lord’s Body is one, and the Lord’s recovery is one. If I gave you “sweet soymilk” to drink every day, it would be easy to say that this is the church, but since I give you “hot and sour soup,” it is not as easy to say that this is the church. When things are palatable for some saints, they speak loudly and highly of the church, but when they taste things that are “hot and spicy,” they often leave and begin to speak differently. If we are thoughtful and our eyes are opened, we will not be easily deceived. We need to know why we are here; otherwise, we will leave this way and come to a dead end.

Those who were with us and then left tried to do another work. Eventually, the work they accomplished became dissipated; it was, at most, a transient success. However, we can testify that Brother Nee was imprisoned for twenty years, and until the time of his departure to be with the Lord, his work was not transient. Even though he is dead, he still speaks, and his words have reached the uttermost parts of the earth. Fifty years ago Brother Nee led me to take this way. I followed him because this way is the Lord’s way. Today, fifty years later, I am happy to say that I am still taking this way. Under the covering of the Lord’s precious blood, I would say that no Christian work can compare with the work of the Lord’s recovery. This work is being spread on all five continents.

It is by the Lord’s mercy and grace that I can say that no other Chinese preacher has had as much influence in preaching the truth and building up the churches among English speakers. I am not even a Galilean fisherman; I am a “fisherman” from Chefoo, which is smaller than Galilee. Peter did not have a theological degree and neither do I, but the Lord’s work among us has truly been blessed.

You are not blind followers, and many of you have received a higher education. If you compare the Life-studies and the other messages put out by this ministry with the books published in Christianity, you will see the preciousness of our publications. When people taste what we are offering, they truly appreciate our “food.” Regrettably, some believers who use our messages are not willing to acknowledge their source.

THERE BEING ONLY ONE WAY
IN THE LORD’S SPREADING TO THE WHOLE EARTH

The Lord is responsible for the spread of His work; it is not us. We are nothing. Even if we earned ten academic degrees, we would not be able to spread the recovery to all five continents. However, we receive letters from all over the world that were written by people inviting us to visit them. Recently, the brothers in South Korea have reminded us to not forget them. If I worked in Europe, I would preach the word every week of the year. Furthermore, Australia and New Zealand are also open to us.

We should not be governed by our feelings, being happy only when we are given “sweet soymilk” and being sad when we are given “hot and sour soup.” Moreover, we should not expect that our service to the Lord will ensure that we have no problems or have a successful career. I have been in the Lord’s work for many years, and I have encountered many problems. I have taken this way whether people commended me or criticized me. The church is the church. We cannot say that the church is no longer the church when a cold wind blows, or that the church is the church when a warm wind blows. In fact, when a cold wind blows, the truth of the church is demonstrated even more. This work has been blessed by the Lord because it has never changed its course based on the direction of the wind.

I have been in the United States for over twenty years, but I have never changed my course. I am not afraid of opposition. I have been speaking for fifty-two years in many places on the earth, but I have not changed my way. We invited Brother T. Austin-Sparks to come to us. He was nearly twenty years my senior, and I greatly respected him. However, when I found out that he was incorrect in his stance toward the Lord’s way, I told him that I could not take his way. Today, twenty years later, everything of his has been relegated to history. Not only is his ministry finished, but his way is no longer practiced. The Lord’s way is the unique way. I am burdened that we all see this matter. I do not want to see the young people coming in today and leaving five years later, neither do I want you to be happy today and disappointed three years later. We must see this way.

Let us use marriage as an illustration. If you are getting married, you must first have a clear knowledge of the one whom you intend to marry. You must not get married foolishly only to divorce later. There is only one Lord, one church, one Body, one Spirit, and one life. Moreover, there is only one way and one fellowship. This is the unique testimony on the island of Taiwan as well as on the whole earth. The Lord has confirmed this. Wherever we go, whether to Africa, South America, or Australia, the testimony among the churches is that we are all in the same move. We have the same life, and we walk on the same way. If we fall into trouble on this way, we should humble ourselves and immediately make a turn, be adjusted, and stop struggling. If we continue our struggling and try to open another way, we will fail.

There is an example in the New Testament. Barnabas led Paul to the apostles in Jerusalem (Acts 9:27), but later, due to his sympathy for his cousin Mark, he separated from Paul (15:37-39). This was related to human affection. From then on, Barnabas is not mentioned in Acts. This is a solemn matter. He did not merely separate from Paul; he diverged from the Lord’s way. If a person has a thought to leave, he must understand that he is not separating from us but from the Lord’s way. Although he is still saved and a child of God, he will come to a dead end regarding his service to the Lord. The Lord’s way is only with His recovery. There is only one way.

EVERYTHING BEING FOR THE BODY OF CHRIST

In taking this way, we must learn not to be proud and not to have personal relationships with others. All the brothers and sisters are precious to us. We are members of the Body, and we should treat everyone equally without discrimination. I frequently contact brothers because of the literature work and because of the responsibility we share in the Lord’s work. But my contact with them is not related to friendship. I do not have any personal bonds of friendship with anyone. Rather, my love is in the Body. Due to the limitation of time, I cannot contact you more often and have a more practical relationship with you. Some of you have written me letters, but I have no time to reply. If you want to receive a reply from me, it is best to write me a note as short as a telegram. It is not that I do not want to read your letters; rather, it is that I do not have the time. Moreover, due to my poor eyesight, I must wait for helpers to read to me.

I love all of you, but I do not have special affection for any of you. I hope that everyone would be like this. Even if you come from the same locality and stay in the same sisters’ house or brothers’ house, you should not consider yourselves as a special group or be distinct from other brothers and sisters. Neither should you have a special feeling toward your locality. Although we cannot be completely void of a special feeling, we should always remember that our work is not for a specific locality. Our work is for the Body of Christ. The fruit of our work is not merely for one local church. The fruit of our work is for the churches throughout the earth.

When you go abroad, you will see that the result of the Lord’s work in Taiwan, whether in Taipei, Taoyuan, or Taichung, affects the United States. Therefore, you should thank and praise the Lord if you are in Taoyuan today, and you should thank and praise the Lord if you are in Taichung tomorrow. Everything is for the Lord’s church, for the family of God. Therefore, whether you are in Taoyuan or Taichung, it is the same; there is no difference. This is a crucial point. Sometimes when we discuss the needs in one locality, the brothers and sisters from that locality speak for their locality. When we discuss the needs in another locality, the brothers and sisters from that locality speak for their locality. It would be beautiful if the brothers and sisters from Hualien spoke for Taichung, not for Hualien, and those from Taichung spoke for Taipei, those from Taipei spoke for Anaheim, those from Anaheim spoke for South Africa, and those from South Africa spoke for Kaohsiung.

We are not here for our own work nor for the church in our own locality. We are here for the Body of Christ. May we be willing to learn this and always remember it. Then we will be preserved to walk this way for our whole life, and we will not have any problems.

In the church we should never be puffed up on behalf of one or be against another. This is like considering Apollos to be higher than Paul or considering Paul to be higher than Cephas. We are all the same. The least among the saints can supply us, and the greatest among the saints can also supply us. Everything is the Lord’s arrangement. We should thank the Lord when He gives us a saint who functions like a big arm. We should thank Him when He gives us a saint who is like a small finger. We should treat everyone alike, without distinction, whether they are weighty, light, high, or low. If your gift is great, you are our brother. If your gift is small, you are still our brother. If you are seemingly not gifted, you are all the more our brother. In this way we will be preserved from many problems. Furthermore, we should never say that we can work with certain ones but not with others. We should be able to work with anyone without expressing our choice. There are always problems when we express our choice.

PRACTICING DIVIDING INTO GROUPS

In relation to our practice, we will fellowship concerning dividing into groups. In the past we formed groups, but we gradually stopped practicing the groups. After observing our situation and studying the practice of other Christian groups, we are clear that a local church must stress meeting in groups. The group is a basic unit.

A church must have groups as its foundation so that the church can take root downward. Likewise, whether or not a church stands firm also depends on the groups. Above the ground we need to raise our standard high, and we need to be rooted with a firm foundation. This foundation is the groups.

The church in Taipei has a total of eleven thousand saints, but only five thousand meet regularly. We need to divide these saints into four hundred groups according to where they reside. Eight or ten saints in a neighborhood should gather as a group. The groups should not be formed according to the spiritual level of the saints nor according to their age. The groups are formed solely according to the geographical location of the saints. Furthermore, once a few saints form a group, there should be no group leader or assistant group leader, nor is there a need for a responsible one or a coordinator. Everyone is equal. This practice is based on our experience. In the past when we assigned group leaders, responsible ones, and coordinators, those who were not assigned felt that they did not have any responsibility. As a result, there were distinctions when the saints functioned in the group. We have to get rid of such concepts. We need to give the saints the impression that, in the Lord’s eyes, everyone in the group is the same. Everyone is precious and useful, and everyone should serve.

In order to advance the groups, we must use the serving ones in the homes, including the full-time and part-time serving ones. We need to have the manpower to advance four hundred groups. In the initial stage we do not have to spend much effort on the gospel in the community. We can wait until we have laid a good and strong foundation in the groups. Then we can preach the gospel in the communities through the groups. The manpower for the community gospel work must first be used to advance the groups.

According to geography, the four hundred groups can be divided into eight districts. Therefore, every district would have fifty groups, with a total of nearly six hundred saints. In the beginning we need to spend more time and invest more manpower into the groups. Our situation can be compared to an old car that has not been in operation for a long time. We are all in the car, but we have to get out and push it. This principle should be adopted in the localities, but we should not be strict in the way that we push.

At present fifty full-timers are assigned to five categories of the work: advancing the group meetings, preaching the gospel in the homes, preaching the gospel in the community, the campus work, and the children’s work. If we are strict and assign ten full-timers to each category of the work, not many will be assigned to advance the groups. Therefore, we need less serving ones in the other categories. If there are fifty groups in a district, there will be a total of five to six hundred saints. We need at least fifty serving ones to advance the groups. In other words, one serving one will work with one group. Every serving one has to be in a group. Before joining the groups, the serving ones must have thorough fellowship and study how to advance the groups. They should study the situation of the meetings, the living situation of the brothers and sisters, and the spiritual level of the groups. Then they should pray together and seek the Lord’s leading to know how to enter into the groups and lead them.

Knowing the Condition of the Groups

We should first know the condition of the groups and then pray to seek a way to lead them. Every group may have a different condition, but in principle it is possible to find the direction to lead the saints. I can give only principles. We should seek the Lord’s leading to fan into flame the gift that is in every member of a group. We should not expect a quick work. The first time we meet with a group, we should give the saints the opportunity to speak freely with one another in a relaxed manner. There is not the need for much prayer. If we try to bring our old way of meeting into the group, we will bring in regulations. For example, although soymilk is delicious, the more we drink it the less we enjoy it. Hence, it is better to let the members of a group feel relaxed. Please do not misunderstand me. Sometimes our piousness in the meeting is a pretense, because we are not necessarily like that in our homes. It is better to be spontaneous. In the group meeting we do not have to pretend, but neither should we be wild.

We can even drink tea in the group meeting so that everyone will relax. Without singing or praying, the serving one can say, “Brothers and sisters, I thank the Lord that we can sit together. The Lord has given the church a new leading, and we have been formed into a group so that we can know one another better, have more fellowship, and can supply and support one another. When I am sick, you will know that I am sick. When you have a problem, I will know that you have a problem. We will be able to sympathize with one another and help one another.” Such a word will help the saints not to pretend. We should keep in mind that having the group meeting is not for us to hold a large worship service in a small meeting. The group meeting is for the saints to enjoy a fresh taste. This taste will help the members of the group to relax. This can be likened to rekindling an old fire with a new flame. In such a meeting it will be easy to fellowship.

Focusing on Reality, Working Aggressively,
and Not Being Anxious

At the beginning of the meeting it is best not to speak too much concerning spiritual matters. We have released many messages. The saints are well fed. They are stout and strong, and there are many things stored within them. Instead of giving them more doctrine or spiritual material, we should give them more reality and an opportunity to speak. We can tell the saints, “The arrangement in the group meeting is different from the arrangement in the past. There is no group leader or coordinator. We all share responsibility for the meeting, and the meetings will not always be in the same home.” Then the saints will be enlivened, the group meeting will be enjoyable, and they will be willing to come again. They might even bring someone to the next meeting. After the saints feel comfortable with the group meeting, we can begin to restore the dormant saints. In brief, the group meeting is the starting point to form a river out of dew. Eventually, there will be a river flowing among us.

We must pray diligently for this matter. In particular, all those who are prepared to serve full time must assist the elders to promote the small groups. The other areas of our work can temporarily slow down. We must remember not to turn the atmosphere in the group meeting into an atmosphere of a small worship service. That is organization. We must be organic. In our service and our work we should always remember to be aggressive but not anxious. It is good if we can achieve something today, and it is also good if we can achieve it tomorrow. We should not be overly concerned with time. However, we must be aggressive and not be loose. This is a principle for receiving the Lord’s blessing.

CHAPTER NINETEEN

THE WAY TO ADVANCE THE SMALL GROUPS

THE CHURCH NEEDING TO ADVANCE THE GROUPS

In the previous message we fellowshipped concerning dividing into groups. The church in Taipei has already formed over four hundred groups. The primary need now is to advance the groups. The church in Taipei currently has about four hundred serving ones, including elders, co-workers, deacons, those who minister the word, coordinators of various services, young full-timers, and part-timers. Every one of these serving ones, whether experienced or not, must be in a group.

From now on the move of the church will be carried out mainly through the groups. The work of the small groups is mainly to restore the dormant saints and to promote the gospel preaching in the homes. Then the groups can promote the gospel work on the college campuses, among the high school and junior high school students, among the children, and in the community. In other words, the foundation of each area of work is the groups. The group is the basic unit and foundation of the church. In order to have a foundation in our work, we must nurture the groups. Once the groups begin to function, every aspect of the work will be carried out smoothly. When the groups function, we can spontaneously bring in dormant saints, and it will be easy for them to be restored. At the same time, we can spread the gospel in the homes. Then we can be aggressive in the gospel work on the campuses, among the children, and in the community. This will result in the multiplication and increase of the church.

Concerning the practice of the group meetings, we are short of experience and personnel, even though we have four hundred groups. This means that every serving one, including the elders and co-workers, should be assigned to help and advance a group. In other words, the serving ones should all serve to advance the groups. If there are not enough serving ones, we should ask other saints to help. For example, the movement of a large truck is slow. If we want it to move faster, it is best to push it. However, as we push it, we will discover that some parts are out of order and defective. Then we can make the necessary repairs so that the truck can run at an ideal speed.

Every serving brother and sister should help in leading a group, but this does not mean that they should regard themselves as a person who is “responsible” for the group. Neither should they consider themselves as a “group leader”; they should take the lead only in regard to fanning the gift within the saints into flame. If the fire in a group has not been kindled, the serving ones should bear responsibility to help kindle the fire. If the fire in a group is dying, the serving ones should fan it into flame. The serving ones should fan the gift in the saints into flame.

DIVIDING INTO GROUPS ACCORDING TO GEOGRAPHY

In forming the groups, there should not be groups for brothers and groups for sisters or groups for elderly saints and groups for younger saints. Neither should there be groups for working saints and groups for students. Rather, the grouping of the saints should be according to geography. If there are eight to ten saints who live close to one another, they should form a group. The members of a group should include brothers, sisters, elderly saints, and younger ones, without any distinction. Even the serving ones should be assigned according to geography. In other words, serving brothers should not be assigned to nurture brothers’ groups, nor should serving sisters be assigned to nurture sisters’ groups. Furthermore, there is no need to consider whether serving saints are suitable for a particular group. They should simply go and work with a group according to geography.

In order to advance the small groups, we must first drop our old concepts. The only factor we should consider in forming groups is geography. There should be no other consideration. This will limit the impact of preconceptions that can frustrate this simple principle of arrangement. This way of arrangement can be compared to the old-fashioned marriages in China in which the husband in an arranged marriage often did not even know what his wife looked like until her veil was lifted. Nevertheless, this way often produced very stable marriages.

Please do not analyze or doubt the benefit that will come from forming groups according to geography. It will help every saint to endeavor to strengthen and supply each group. After much consideration before the Lord, we believe that we should take this way. We have eaten much of the tree of the knowledge of good and evil, and our eyes are opened (Gen. 3:7). When our eyes are so “open” about certain matters, we often hesitate to act. For example, a person who knows everything about the preparation of food is often reluctant to eat food prepared by others because he is afraid of eating food prepared using unhygienic methods. It is better to be blind.

The eyes of some of the younger elders and co-workers are too open. When I propose something, some of them immediately begin to think of possible complications in how to carry it out. For example, before the meeting I said that we needed four hundred brothers and sisters to help the small groups. Immediately, a brother asked whether sisters should lead only sisters’ groups and not lead brothers’ groups. This brother has too many considerations. Having eyes that are so open makes advancement difficult.

The principle for arranging the small groups is by geography. We should not say that it is difficult to lead a group that has more older saints. Neither is it necessary to ask an elderly sister to help with a group of elderly sisters. Such thoughts are wrong. Instead, it is possible for an elderly sister to lead young sisters and for a young sister to lead a group of elderly sisters.

We do not agree with special arrangements. When we make arrangements by anything other than geography, we are no longer according to the principle of an old-fashioned Chinese marriage, that is, “a match made in heaven.” When heaven acts as the matchmaker to put a couple together, it is the best match. Therefore, the elders should not be involved in grouping the saints and the serving ones together in any way other than geography. The church in Taipei has over twenty meeting halls and around five thousand saints who meet regularly. These saints have been divided into more than four hundred groups. Some halls are larger, and others are smaller. Some halls may have only eight or ten groups. These four hundred groups should be divided into eight districts, and every district should have fifty groups. We must still study how to combine the groups into districts for the advance of the Lord’s move.

We have not yet reached the stage of forming districts. We first need to advance the groups. After the groups begin to function, the elders and co-workers should combine the groups to form districts. Every district should have fifty groups. Then ten to twenty elders and co-workers should encourage the districts. This is similar to pushing an old car. Initially, many people are needed to push it, but once the old car starts moving, those who were pushing can take care of other matters. In the same principle, once the groups begin to function, we will not need four hundred serving ones to push them. We will probably need no more than a hundred serving ones to nurture them.

DEMONSTRATING HOW TO ADVANCE THE SMALL GROUPS

We should demonstrate and explain how to advance the group meetings. Suppose a co-worker goes to lead and nurture a small group in which there are many sisters but only a few brothers. This co-worker should not give a long message; rather, he should consider the saints as a family and greet them with an intimate concern. He should also be aware of long pauses or gaps to avoid a dull and heavy atmosphere.

As a result of our meeting habits, many co-workers and elders like to formalize the small group meetings as if they are conducting a worship service. To them, a group meeting is merely a large meeting held with fewer people. If we eat the same food continually, even if it is good food, we will grow to dislike it. We are famous for having numerous church meetings. Our meetings can be compared to eating, and just as we need to eat three meals a day, we need to meet frequently. But if we eat dumplings three times a day for six months, dumplings will no longer be our favorite food. According to my understanding, nine out of ten saints come to the meetings only out of habit. Therefore, we must avoid bringing in the atmosphere of a large meeting into a small group meeting. In particular, we must avoid the habit of giving a message.

The most important part of a small group meeting is its beginning. We should not consider what to say at the beginning of the meeting. An opening word damages the meeting. A group meeting does not need an opening word, and it does not need our conventional way of meeting. Instead, we should chat with the brothers and sisters. The secret is to not consider the meeting as a special kind of meeting. We should simply be as if we are at home and chatting with the members of our family. There is no need to prepare a special topic for conversation. Once we prepare something, we ruin the meeting. We either fall into a worship service or mere formality. We might ask a saint, whom we have not met before, his name. We can also ask the saints about their interests, but we should be careful not to hold general conversations about things like the weather. Neither should the conversation center on one person; rather, everyone should be brought into the conversation. This is not a small matter; our ability to nurture a small group depends on such matters.

Our conversation with the saints should not be aimless. Perhaps after ten minutes of conversing, we will come to a turning point. At this juncture we can achieve our goal in leading the group by stirring up the saints. We should perfect them to serve. We should stir up their burden to restore the dormant saints. We should promote the gospel in the homes. We should also promote the community gospel.

We should not let the conversations continue aimlessly. Our purpose is to know the spiritual condition of the saints and then to fan into flame the gift that is within them. This depends on our skill and our spiritual sense. We need wisdom in the things we do. For example, it would be inappropriate to say, “Our desire is not merely to get to know one another. It is more important for us to fan the gift within you into flame so that you are stirred up to serve the Lord.” Such a speaking will be counterproductive.

We can compare the group meetings to playing basketball. After we dribble the ball, we must throw it into the basket. In other words, our conversation in the small group can be compared to dribbling a ball. At a certain point we should aim at the basket to make a score. We should not speak doctrine. On the contrary, we should exercise wisdom to lead the saints into the practical burdens for advancing the small group.

This is easy to say but not so easy to carry out. We often have meetings with no result, because we continually dribble the ball, but no one takes a shot at the basket.
